Kunshan 93

The Head of the Autonomous Experimental District Resigns

Townspeople Jointly Telegraph to Retain Him

Zhu Wenyuan, the head of the autonomous experimental district, has been handling local autonomy with outstanding achievements. Especially during the January 28th Incident, he never left his post, and the local area benefited a lot. Afterwards, the people were grateful for his righteousness and bravery, and specially built a pavilion and erected a monument in front of the district office (Lu Jia Bang Town) to commemorate him. Recently, the district head cited financial difficulties and difficult handling of affairs, and submitted his resignation to County Magistrate Peng in person on the 2nd of this month. The townspeople were alarmed when they heard the news, and 42 people, including Zhang Zhifang and Zhu Qijia, jointly telegraphed the county government to retain him.

Changshu 94

The County Government Moves to a New Address

The current office location of the county government is rented from the Zeng family for a monthly rent of 180 yuan. Last year, the county government sold the old office base on Daonan Street and built a new county office on Dongmen Street. Gong Fengji's workshop won the bid to build it, and construction began in May of last year. It has now been completed, and the internal lighting and decoration have also been completed. The county government has decided to start moving to the new address for office on the 6th of this month, and has started to sort out documents and move gradually from now on. The new office building is spacious, and in addition to the separate offices for each department, the secretaries, clerks, guards, and dormitories all have their own dedicated rooms. It is estimated that the relocation can be completely completed in late this month.

The County Public Security Bureau Holds a Police Affairs Meeting 95

The County Public Security Bureau convened more than 20 people, including the chiefs of each branch bureau and the patrol officers of the branch stations, for a police affairs meeting in the afternoon of the 5th. The resolutions are as follows: (1) During the winter prevention period, gambling is strictly prohibited, and gambling for the gods in various villages is banned. It is also necessary to strictly prohibit the bad habit of gambling during the first five days of the abolished New Year. Warn the heads of the Baojia in various villages and townships and the village and town chiefs. (2) This month is the general accounting period, and there are more disputes, and it is inevitable that some unscrupulous people will block the road and rob. Each branch bureau and station should adopt a patrol system to maintain the business flag. (3) During the New Year, the old customs of worshipping gods and ancestors and setting off firecrackers are often still used, which is not only easy to cause misunderstandings, but also easy to catch fire, and should be banned. (4) Recently, due to the weather and the drought, various shift rounds and ships often do not depart on time or carry more passengers, which can easily cause accidents. They should be checked and banned at any time to maintain traffic.

Wuxi 96

Appealing for Relief for Primary School Expenses The tuition fees for each primary school in this county are stipulated by the bureau to be 80 yuan per semester for each grade. If the amount collected is insufficient, the principal must make up for it. Recently, the principals of various primary schools have stated that at this time of rural economic bankruptcy, coupled with the drought, the harvest is hopeless, and it is extremely difficult to collect tuition fees. The tuition fees collected this winter solstice are less than 50% of the bureau's budget of 80 yuan per grade, which is a huge difference. If all the principals make up for it, it will inevitably be impossible to maintain. Therefore, the County Education Association convened a temporary executive committee meeting yesterday and resolved to submit a request to the County Education Bureau for prompt relief.

The Armed Police Department Sends Personnel to Interrogate the Poison Pill Case 97

The Zhenjiang Armed Police Headquarters previously received the case of Miao Kunrong, who was guilty of selling poison pills, and the case of Guo Xiyuan, which were presented by the county government of this county, requesting interrogation, verification, and sentencing. After receiving the presentation, the department sent Military Judge Jia Huanchen to Wuxi yesterday to conduct interrogation at the county government. The political police were ordered to separately summon the witnesses in the two cases, including Wu Baolin and Guo Yongkang, to the case for interrogation at 3 pm. After the interrogation, each was ordered to provide a written guarantee and dismissed. Jia returned to the province that evening to report his mission.

Regulations on the Collection Method of Business Tax 98

The Jiangsu Provincial Finance Department stipulates that the business tax in this province was originally scheduled to be collected every quarter, starting on the first day of the first month and ending on the last day of the last month. It has now been revised to start collecting on the first day of the first month and end on the last day of the second month. Commercial firms that fail to pay within the deadline will be charged a late payment penalty of 20%. Those who fail to pay within two months of the deadline will be suspended from business. For short-term businesses, the business tax bureau will determine the deadline at any time, and those who fail to pay within the deadline will be suspended from business. All business taxes for the spring season of the 24th year are about to be collected, and should be handled uniformly. Yesterday, a special order was issued to the business tax bureaus of each county to comply. After receiving the order, the business tax bureau of this county has already issued a notice to all commercial firms for reference. Changzhou

Local News

Shanghai-Guangdong Sightseeing Flight 107

Returned Midway Yesterday Due to Fog

Arrived Safely in Wenzhou at 9:00 am and Circled the City Before Heavy Fog Covered It. The Northbound Plane Was Also Blocked. Excellent Coastal Scenery, Flight into the Picture. The China National Aviation Corporation recently purchased several of the latest Douglas seaplanes from the United States for the purpose of restoring the Shanghai-Guangdong flight route. The first one was piloted by the Salas pilot, and on the 5th, it made a test flight from Shanghai, and arrived safely in Guangzhou at 2:30 pm that day. The other Douglas plane, Fujian, was piloted by pilot Fang Si, and five Chinese and foreign journalists were invited. At 7:00 am yesterday morning, it took off from Shanghai to visit Fujian and Guangdong. At 9:00 am, it arrived safely in Wenzhou. At 11:00 am, it flew towards Fuzhou. Unexpectedly, the weather changed suddenly midway, and the heavy fog was overwhelming. It had no choice but to return to Wenzhou. Waiting until 1:30 pm, the weather between Fuzhou and Xiamen was still bad. It had no choice but to fly back to Shanghai. At 3:30 pm, it landed at Longhua Airport. It will continue to fly when the coastal weather turns better. The details are described below:

Inviting the Press to Visit Along the Route 108

The China National Aviation Corporation used the latest Douglas aircraft to fly on the Shanghai-Guangdong route, and officially took passengers from the 8th. In order to make the outside world understand the flight safety, it specially invited the Chinese and Western press, including Qian Hua of Shenbao, Wang Jiao of Shen Shi Telegraph Agency, Ms. Luo Qian of Zi Linbao Western Newspaper, Paul of The Times, and Gold of Damei Evening News. At 7:00 am yesterday morning, American pilot Fang Si and telegraph operator Mr. Chen drove the Douglas Fujian aircraft from Longhua Airport. The company's general manager, Mr. Dai Enji, also took the same plane to take care of everything and inspect the business situation of each航站顺道.

Comfortable Equipment, Soaring into the Sky 109

The Douglas seaplane has two engines on the left and right. The upper part of the wing is painted yellow. There are six passenger seats inside. The chairs can be shaken and the backrests can be lowered for passengers to take a nap. It is very comfortable. Luggage is placed in the tail and equipped with a radio transceiver. During the flight, the noise of the plane is not very loud because of the sound insulation equipment. Passengers boarded the plane from the floating dock. At 7:00 am, the pilot turned on the engine and drove slowly along the Huangpu River, gradually increasing speed. After two minutes, the speed increased even more, the waves hit the windows, and finally soared into the sky, circling and flying south.

Crossing Hangzhou Bay and Out of the Coastline 110

Flying for only five minutes, it arrived at Hangzhou Bay. The river water was like a belt, the fields were like chess pieces, and the villages were sparsely located, embellished among them. Approaching the coast, from the salt field to the bay, before long, it was a vast expanse. The sea was as flat as a mirror, and the fishing boats dotted the sea. The feeling was very refreshing. In 20 minutes, it reached the Zhoushan Islands. Overlooking the small islands, they were scattered like stars and chess pieces. The terrain was extremely dangerous and the currents were turbulent, making navigation extremely difficult. At 7:40 am, it reached Zhenhai at the entrance of Ningbo. The mountains overlapped and flew over, with the tops of the mountains below the feet. The flight followed the ups and downs of the mountains. The fields were crisscrossed, with green and yellow interspersed. The smoke from the villages was like entering a picture. At 8:00 am, the flight had reached one hour. The pilot reported that he had traveled 155 miles. Before long, it reached Shibu, passed Haimen, and then reached Wenzhou, which was exactly 9:00 am, 270 miles from Shanghai. The plane circled the city once and slowly landed on the river surface.

Wenzhou Welcomes Tourists to Tour the City 111

The China National Aviation Corporation set up a simple floating station in Jiangxin, Wenzhou. Representatives from various institutions and groups were already waiting at the station to welcome them. They shook hands and welcomed them to have tea and snacks in the house. After the plane was refueled, the local representatives were invited to try the ride. The invitees included County Magistrate Xie Yong, President of the Local Court Yang Shuyou, Postmaster Xiang Ding, Telegraph Bureau Chief Yang Ding, Bank of China President Chen Tinggao, Zhejiang Ou Daily President Li Guodong, and Wenzhou gentry and merchants Yang Yunong and Lv Weizhou, etc., more than 30 people. A total of five flights were made around Wenzhou, and all were satisfied. At the same time, Mr. Dai Enji and the Chinese and Western journalists were accompanied by Yang Zhonghe, a staff member of the company's Wenzhou station, and took a small boat to cross the river and land on the shore. They took rickshaws and toured the city. At 10:30 am, they returned to the floating station and took off at 11:00 am, heading straight for Fuzhou.

Heavy Fog Returns Midway 112

Flying to 11:40 am, thick fog came to the face. In an instant, overlooking the mountains and seas, it was a blank. It was dark and light, and the telegraph operator received a radio report that the weather in Fuzhou, Xiamen, and Shantou was bad. The plane that flew north from Guangzhou did not reach Shantou and also returned to Guangzhou due to fog. So it returned to Wenzhou. At 12:30 pm, it returned to Wenzhou and waited for a weather report from Fuzhou. However, there was no news of improvement. There was no suitable accommodation in Wenzhou, so it was temporarily decided to return to Shanghai. At 1:30 pm, it left Wenzhou and landed safely at Longhua Airport at 3:30 pm. The flight lasted seven and a half hours. Mr. Dai Enji and others provided warm hospitality along the way, and the pilot and telegraph operator reported flight information and provided various conveniences at any time. Special thanks should be expressed.

Italian First Ambassador Wen Shenzuo

Arrived in Shanghai Today 113

Zhang Naiyan, Shen Yi, and Others Return to China on the Same Ship. Various Chinese and Italian Institutions Sent Personnel to Welcome Them. Italian Honorary Medals Were Awarded to Jiang and Wang Xinxin News Agency Reported: Wen Shenzuo, the first Italian Ambassador to China, has set off for China on the Italian postal ship Contello Soso. The ship is scheduled to arrive in port at about 11:00 am today. At that time, all circles in China and Italy will go to the port to welcome him. After arriving in Shanghai, Mr. Wen will rest for a while and then set a date to enter Beijing to meet with Chairman Lin and present his credentials. The details are recorded as follows:

Arrive in Shanghai This Afternoon, Zhang and Shen Come Together 114

The Contello Soso is scheduled to arrive here at about 11:00 am today and berth at the Broadway Road Gonghexang Wharf. Periodic Trip to the Capital to Present Credentials 115

After Mr. Wen arrives in Shanghai, he will rest briefly and await the Chinese government's confirmation of the date for meeting the Chairman. Then, he will proceed to the capital to present his credentials as ambassador and pay courtesy calls to Chinese foreign affairs officials. As for the former Italian envoy to China, Mr. Bonifacio Pignatti Morano di Custoza, he will accompany Mr. Wen to the capital to present credentials and then depart from Shanghai on the Italian postal ship Conte Rosso on the 15th to return to his country. It is also understood that Mr. Wen brought with him a specially made Grand Cross of the Order of Merit of the Italian Republic, to be awarded to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek and President Wang Jingwei. This medal is the highest honor in Italy.

A Brief Biography of Ambassador Vincenzo Arangio Ruiz 116

Ambassador Vincenzo Arangio Ruiz is currently 50 years old and holds a doctorate from the University of Palermo. He has served as a secretary in the Italian embassies in the United Kingdom and Portugal and was once a captain in the infantry. He also participated in Mussolini's March on Rome, earning Mussolini's trust. In 1924, he was appointed Director-General of Tax Affairs at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. In 1929, he was promoted to Ambassador to Turkey, providing strong support to the newly emerging Turkey and making outstanding contributions to improving Italian-Turkish relations. After the elevation of Sino-Italian diplomatic relations, he was appointed as the first Italian ambassador to China. Mr. Arangio Ruiz is very familiar with the situation in the Far East, and it is expected that after taking office, he will be able to promote closer ties between China and Italy.

Notice of Launch 121

San Bei Company Announces: To Whom It May Concern: Our company's Ningxing steamship has been operating on the Shanghai-Ningbo route for many years, with the sole purpose of facilitating the travel of passengers and the transportation of goods in the Ningbo area. Recently, the rural economy has been declining, and Ningbo's taxation on agricultural exports as a commercial port has been greatly affected. In addition, highways in various counties of Ningbo are gradually opening to traffic. In order to assist the rural areas of Ningbo and in line with the principle of facilitating transportation, our company has invested heavily in building wharves and warehouses in Zhenhai, connecting them to the county and provincial roads. We have added the Mingxing steamship to open the Shanghai-Zhenhai route, also covering Wan and Ningbo. All local products imported and exported on the Shanghai-Zhenhai route will be exempt from taxes, with the approval of the Inspectorate General of Customs, in order to provide a lifeline for the farmers of Ningbo. Passengers from Ningbo will save time and money. We hope that people from all walks of life in Ningbo will pay attention. Furthermore, the Mingxing steamship employs attendants and has fixed service fees included in the ticket price, which will be strictly enforced. The launch is imminent. We hereby announce.

Implemented Today 122

From then on, each trip from Shanghai to Ningbo and from Ningbo to Shanghai will also cover Wan and Zhenhai. At the same time, the newly purchased Mingxing steamship will make its maiden voyage from Shanghai to Zhenhai on the 9th, also covering Wan and Ningbo. All passenger tickets and fares will be the same as the old prices for the Shanghai-Ningbo route. Major internal renovations have been made, and there will be no predatory competition.

Post Office Begins Crackdown on Private Postal Agencies 125

Post Office Suddenly Orders Detention of Private Mails

The Weighing Regulation Abolished

Private Mail Businesses Still Make a Final Stand

Weighing Regulation Abolished 126

Da Gong News Agency reports that the National Postal Administration of the Ministry of Communications, due to the failure of private postal agencies to comply with the order to close down, has abolished the weighing regulation and has ordered the detention of all private mails to and from South China, North China, the Yangtze River area, and inland ports. The National Private Postal Agencies Association is awaiting instructions from the central government before making a final stand. Details are as follows: In order to preliminarily restrict the private postal agencies, the Ministry of Communications, considering that their operations disrupt the postal system, promulgated the Provisional Weighing Regulation for Private Mail in 1929. Initially, a weighing fee of 20 cents was charged per pound, which was gradually increased to 75 cents and 95 cents. In 1933, it was increased to $1.25 per pound. In April of last year, it was changed to a fee of 10 cents for every two ounces of mail, totaling $1.65 per pound. After the Ministry of Communications increased the weighing fee every year, the private postal agencies could not bear the burden, and private postal agencies across the country could not maintain their operations, and 15 percent closed down. This regulation was originally a temporary measure to restrict private postal agencies. Now that private postal agencies have been restricted to close down by the end of last year, this regulation is no longer necessary. Therefore, the National Postal Administration has issued a notice to all post offices to abolish it. If private mail is found again, it will be detained and punished as private delivery of letters.

Private Mails Detained in Various Places 127

For the sake of their own survival and the livelihood of tens of thousands of employees, the National Private Postal Agencies Association is still making a final appeal to the Ministry of Communications regarding the deadline order. The central authorities have not yet issued a formal order on whether to ban or allow them to exist. Therefore, private postal businesses are still operating as usual. However, in order to implement the ban, the post office has detained all private mails to and from various places since December 30th of last year. A reporter from Da Gong News Agency inquired at the Shanghai Private Mail Association about the detained letters yesterday. In South China, this includes Wenzhou, Fuzhou, Xiamen, You Tou, Guangzhou. In the Yangtze River area, this includes Hankou, Jiujiang, Wuhu, Anqing, Nanjing, Zhenjiang, Shanghai. In North China, this includes Tianjin, Beiping, Shijiazhuang, Zhengzhou, Jinan. In the inland, such as Wuxi, Suzhou, Hangzhou, and other major ports, all incoming and outgoing private mails have now been detained.

Private Postal Businesses Make a Final Stand 128

A reporter from Da Gong News Agency went to the north and south districts of the city and the concession yesterday to investigate the situation of the private postal agencies. The entrances were deserted, and the contrast with the past was overwhelming. When asked, the person in charge of the Private Mail Association replied that private postal businesses across the country still hope that the government will understand the difficulties of the people and withdraw the order to ban them. However, the central government has not yet issued any instructions. Therefore, they are still operating as usual. If the government does not give a satisfactory reply in the future, they will convene a general meeting to make a final stand.

The Anxiety of Senders 129

Furthermore, according to general opinion, the post office should first take fundamental measures to ban private postal agencies before stopping them from accepting and sending private mails. It should not detain the letters that have already been sent halfway. Generally, merchants and civilians send letters for convenience. Some believe that private postal agencies are more convenient and therefore abandon the post office and go to private postal agencies. Before the private postal agencies petition the government and before the government has issued instructions, they still send mails as usual. The post office should not detain the letters, as it is making things difficult for the senders. It is like the saying "eating at the neighbor's door and thanking the neighbor across the street," which is not a good way to do things.

Liquidator Speaks 132

Moreover, at the end of last year, the Hong Kong head office telegraphed requesting a remittance of a certain amount, but the manager of the Shanghai branch, in order to protect the depositors here, did not grant the request. As for the accounts, because the closure occurred on the day after the New Year's holiday, the accounts for last year had already been settled, and the accounts for this year only covered one day, January 4, so the inspection is very convenient. It should be possible to announce the balance sheet of the branch in about three or four days.

These depositors, totaling about $120,000 to $130,000, were relatively calm, only saying that they hoped to reach a conclusion before the end of the lunar year so that they could get funds. There are very few depositors with several thousand or several hundred dollars, and they have not yet taken any action. If there are losses as a result of the liquidation, priority will be given to repaying the savings deposits of depositors.

Huang Zigang Petitioned 134

To Undertake the Transfer and Delivery Bureau, Original Transfer of Mail in the Four Northeastern Provinces is Purely a Private Business, Says Central News Agency. The three businesses of various mails and packages, remittances, etc., to and from the four provinces of Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, and Rehe, will be transferred by the Shanhaiguan and Gubeikou Transfer and Delivery Bureau from January 10th and February 1st respectively. The previous report details the situation, but what is the internal organization of the so-called Transfer and Delivery Bureau? This is what the people of the country want to know. A reporter learned from reliable sources that the so-called Transfer and Delivery Bureau is purely a private business undertaken by retired postal worker Huang Zigang. We have found Huang Zigang's petition to undertake the business as follows: To Petition: The northeastern four provinces are rich in land, and hundreds of thousands of compatriots from within the pass go to the northeast to reclaim land and do business every year. The funds remitted back to the pass each year amount to more than ten million dollars. In the past, they were all remitted by the post office. The goods sent out of the pass by parcel post through the post office were also numerous. Since the September 18th Incident, our government, based on the great plan of the nation, resolutely blockaded postal services in the northeast. Three years have passed, and international opinions have shifted. However, considering that the compatriots outside the pass are in a desperate situation, postal delivery is blocked, parcels are cut off, and remittances are suspended, the impact on the balance of the national economy and the flow of goods and financial information is not small. The pain of the people living outside the pass and their relatives and friends within the pass is even more imaginable. I, Zigang, have served in the post office for 20 years. Although I am retired, I have the country and the people in my heart. I always cherish the great wish to strive for a win-win solution between the great plan of our government and the interests of the people. At Shanhaiguan and Gubeikou, I will organize a Transfer and Delivery Bureau as a merchant to transfer incoming and outgoing letters and parcels and remittances, charging commissions to cover expenses. All matters that should be handled by Zigang will be handled responsibly, and I am willing to provide a guarantee and sign a contract to show good faith. Respectfully submitted to the Postal Administration, Huang Zigang. It is heard that after receiving Huang Zigang's petition, the Postal Administration has ordered the Hebei Management Bureau to contact and negotiate the contract to undertake the business.

Jianghai Customs Issued Two Announcements Yesterday 135

Imported Alcohol Subject to Unified Tax, Solicitation of Bids for Artificial Coarse Silk Announcement 1: Jianghai Customs issued Announcement No. 1417 yesterday, stating: Now, in accordance with the order of the Ministry of Finance, from January 1, 1935, imported alcohol, in addition to import duties, shall be subject to unified tax. The tax rates are as follows: Ordinary alcohol: 13 cents of national currency per kilogram. Denatured alcohol and wood alcohol (including refined coconut wine and fusel oil): 6.5 cents of national currency per liter. Alcohol that has already paid the unified tax and is transported to areas where the unified tax has already been implemented shall be exempt from transit tax. Merchants are hereby notified.

Announcement 2: The Customs also announced that the Customs currently has 21,300 pounds of artificial coarse silk for sale by tender. Bidders can go to the Transportation Department to view samples and obtain order forms. Bids must be submitted to the General Affairs Section of the Tax Department before 10:00 AM on the 11th of this month (Sunday). The Customs reserves the right not to accept the highest bid or any bid. The winning bidder shall pay 25% of the bid price to the Customs on the same day and pay the price and take delivery of the goods within one week. This is hereby announced.

Zhuang Xueben Returned to Shanghai After Surveying the Borderlands 136

Talks About the Customs and Culture of the Golok Region

National News Agency reports that Mr. Zhuang Xueben, a special commissioner for northwest surveying of the Northwest Development Association, followed Mr. Huang Musong, a special envoy sent to pay respects to the Dalai Lama, to various places on the border of Sichuan in March of last year to conduct surveys. After arriving in Chengdu, Mr. Zhuang parted ways with Mr. Huang and, together with a translator and two attendants, traveled at his own expense to the wild regions bordering the provinces of Western Sichuan, Qinghai, Gansu, and Sichuan, risking danger to conduct surveys. He passed through Guanxian, Wenchuan, Lifan, Wutun, Sidu, Aba, grasslands, and arrived at Golok, where he stayed for two months. Then, he followed the Yellow River eastward to Songpan, and then went south along the Minjiang River, spending six months in total, going deep into barren lands, climbing mountains and wading through rivers, enduring extreme hardship. He took many photos and left Chengdu on December 18th to return to Beijing, arriving in Shanghai on New Year's Day this year. Yesterday at 4 PM, colleagues from the Pudong Qichangzhan Security Corps held a banquet to congratulate Mr. Zhuang on his success and to listen to his narration of the survey process. Zhang Mingqin, Xu Baoming, Shen Xingyuan, Zhang Zaibo, Li Guanlin, Hu Baizhou, Chen Fusheng, Wu Zilong, Huang Jingwan, Zhu Shuren, Shen Xingyuan, and others, more than 60 people, attended. During the banquet, Mr. Zhuang spoke about his journey, saying, "The place I visited this time, with Golok as the end point, has never been visited by Han Chinese, so there is very little description in our country's history and geography. Even if there is, it is not detailed. Golok has more than 100,000 people, all of whom are extremely uncivilized. Their property consists only of cattle and sheep, and money is useless. Therefore, I (Zhuang claims himself) bought many pieces of cloth early and exchanged them for things after entering the area. After that, I relied on this to survive. Men, except for being soldiers and hunting, specialize in stealing other people's cattle and sheep, which has almost become a habit. Women have extremely high rights and can order men at any time. All housework is handled by them. In the morning, they take all the cattle and sheep to places with water and grass and return at noon, then milk them and cook, and eat with their husbands. The main food is beef and mutton, and the way of eating is very strange, and most of them eat it half raw. These people like to drink Sichuan twig tea, selling about 30,000 packets a year, more than 100 catties per packet. They wear a sheepskin jacket, regardless of the hot summer or cold winter, they never wash or change it. They wear it during the day and use it as a quilt at night. When it's hot, they are all naked, their upper bodies are covered with sweat and grease, and they smell bad. The wives of the chieftains are very extravagant, with hair crowns made of agate and coral, and their whole bodies are covered in silk, worth at least more than 10,000 yuan. Their residences are tents made of yak hair ropes, and they all sleep in the same place, regardless of whether they are masters or servants. The people are born with iron muscles and bones, and they are not afraid of wind, frost, rain, or snow. Sometimes they even sleep in the open on the grass, and they rarely get sick. They rely entirely on cattle and horses for transportation, and their skills are very high. They all believe in Lamaism. If there are four sons in a family, they must send two to study Lamaism. These people specialize in chanting scriptures for people and live a good life. Among them, the living Buddha is the most revered. Every move he makes is regarded as a god. When he goes out for a walk, the people all prostrate themselves on the side of the road and hope that the living Buddha will whip them on the back, saying that this will eliminate all sins in their lives. Some people even take the excrement and urine of the living Buddha home and eat it, saying that this can prolong life. There is a living Buddha who is more than 130 years old, who came from a beggar. Because he was extremely poor and bored, he went around spreading rumors and claiming that he was powerful and could cure all diseases. He actually gained the support of many people, so he became tyrannical and openly married a wife and a concubine and had more than a dozen daughters. Marriage is extremely free in the Golok region. At the end of each year, a large number of men and women gather and choose freely. If both parties agree, they can marry. The selection must also be appropriate. The son of a chieftain must marry the daughter of a chieftain, which has almost become a law. If there is no suitable partner for a while, they will choose one from the sisters of their mother to marry. Some people, fearing that their family property will be dispersed, have several brothers marry one wife together. The date of cohabitation is determined by the woman. Whoever's turn it is on a certain day, the rest will go out to work. The first son is called the eldest brother the father, and the second son is called the second brother the father, and the rest are called uncles, so there are never any disputes. When a person dies, they are usually sky buried, and the corpse is thrown naked into the wilderness for birds to peck at. The nobles are mostly cremated. The people despise the Han Chinese," and so on. Then, Zhang Mingqin, Hu Baizhou, Huang Jingwan, and others gave speeches of encouragement, and the banquet ended at about 10 o'clock. Finally, Mr. Zhuang told the reporter that he had collected very detailed information about the customs and culture of the Golok region and took many photos. He plans to write a special book for those who study border issues to refer to. If there is an opportunity, he plans to risk danger again to survey the barren lands of Yunnan, Qinghai, and Mongolia, but this is beyond the financial resources of an individual. He hopes that compatriots can provide material and spiritual assistance to achieve his humble wishes. He is especially grateful to Mr. Huang Jingwan and Mr. Hu Baizhou for their assistance in this trip to Sichuan. He will think of ways to contribute to the country and society in the future and live up to everyone's expectations. Finally, he hopes that young people across the country will travel more to the borderlands and not just shout to go to the northwest while clinging to the pleasures of the city. At this time when the national crisis is deepening, the border situation is what we urgently want to know. As citizens, we should fulfill our civic obligations. If the government can find ways to encourage us, then cooperation between the government and the people will bring a lot of help to the development of the northwest in the future.

Relief Association for Drought Disasters Distributed 500,000 in Relief Funds to Various Provinces Yesterday 139

Also Released Income and Expenditure Reports From Last Year to the Present

Xu Shiying and Others Launched a Rural Loan Group

The Shanghai Relief Association for Drought Disasters in Various Provinces convened its fifth plenary meeting of standing committee members at the Renji Hall yesterday afternoon at 4 PM to continue distributing relief funds to disaster areas.

Attending Committee Members 140

The standing committee members present included Xu Shiying, Zhu Xiechen, Wang Dizhai, Wang Xiaolai, Xu Xiajun, Qu Wenliu, Zhao Yiwu, Li Dachao, Wu Tiecheng (Li Dachao as proxy), Huang Tao, Lin Kanghou, Huang Bodu, Wang Yiting, Chen Zhonggao, Du Yuesheng (Zhai Yanfang), Huang Ruisheng, Chen Liangyu, Zhai Yanfang, Li Zizai, Zhao Jinqing, Huang Hanzhi, Guan Jiongzhi, Wang Shaocheng (Peng Yunling), Liu Wanqing, Peng Yunling, Yin Guanzhi, Qian Jinping, Mao Yun, Wen Lanting, Zhang Lanping, Wu Yansong, Chen Jicheng, and others, more than 30 people. Xu Shiying presided over the meeting.

Disaster Relief Fund Allocation 141

(1) Regarding the proposal to continue allocating disaster relief funds to various provinces, it was resolved that: Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hunan, and Hubei each receive 70,000 (dollars), Jiangsu receives 40,000, Henan and Hebei each receive 20,000, Sichuan receives 50,000, and Guangxi receives 15,000 (totaling 495,000). The remaining 5,000 is allocated to Shaanxi, Gansu, and Putian County in Fujian (three locations). (2) Regarding the proposal that all the aforementioned disaster relief funds must be distributed to the disaster victims within this year, it was resolved to pass the motion. (3) Regarding the proposal that honest and impartial personnel should be sent to the disaster areas for inspection during the distribution of disaster relief funds, it was resolved that the inspection personnel should be jointly appointed by Xu Shiying, Wen Lanting, Wang Yiting, Qu Wenliu, Huang Hanzhi, and others. (4) Regarding the proposal that additional disaster relief funds should be allocated to Anhui and Hunan provinces due to the severe disaster situation and once widespread donations are received, it was resolved to pass the motion.

Revenue and Expenditure of Funds 142

The association also released a report on revenue and expenditure from the date of its establishment last year to January 4th of this year. The details are as follows: Under the revenue section, donations amounted to $280,606.90, and the Winter Emergency Relief Committee for Disaster Areas allocated $50,000, totaling $330,606.90 in revenue. Under the expenditure section: $19,000 was allocated to the Jiaxu Zhejiang Disaster Relief Association for designated donors, $4,000 was allocated to the Hubei Native Place Association in Shanghai for the Hengshe Society, a fundraising committee for drought and flood disasters in the province, $20,000 was issued for Hubei disaster relief, $61,172 was issued for Jiangsu disaster relief (of which $1,172 was from designated donors), $20,000 was issued for Jiangxi disaster relief, $64,139.60 was issued for Zhejiang disaster relief, $20,000 was issued for Hunan disaster relief, 5,732 bags of American wheat were purchased, $12,610.04 was allocated to Zhejiang (deducted from disaster relief funds), $5,000 was allocated to the Capital Joint Winter Relief Association, $1,000 was allocated to the Qingjiangpu Congee Factory for expenses, $200 was allocated to the Nanjing Red Swastika Society for a congee factory for disaster victims, $80 was allocated to the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau for the repatriation of Hubei refugees, $110 was allocated to the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau for the repatriation of Anhui and Henan refugees, $1,000 was issued for Anhui disaster inspection expenses, $2,000 was issued for Hubei disaster inspection expenses, $100 was issued for Hebei disaster inspection expenses, $60 was issued for Henan disaster inspection expenses, $1,249.40 was spent on advertising fees, $381.16 was spent on printing fees, $51.58 was spent on packing fees for disaster relief clothing, $54 was spent on rent (for disaster relief warehouse), $47.10 was spent on flags and badges for disaster relief, totaling $232,255.24 in expenditures, with a remaining balance of $98,351.66.

Rural Loans 143

The Drought Disaster Relief Association, led by Xu Shiying and others, initiated a proposal for the Shanghai banking community to organize a rural loan group. Yesterday, they published an outline and explanation, stating: "Our country has always been known for its agricultural foundation. In recent decades, internal turmoil has been incessant, governance has been complicated, and taxes have been heavy, leaving the people without a stable existence. Nearly all the money in rural areas has flowed into government offices and cities, and has been exported abroad. Imports exceed exports, and there has been no development of gold and silver mines. The limited resources are on the verge of depletion. Furthermore, successive years of droughts and floods, and the rampant activities of communist bandits, have reduced those with average wealth to extreme poverty, and have turned the extremely poor into bandits. Without immediate relief, the total collapse of society is imminent and unavoidable. Last year, Mr. Zhang Gongquan of the Bank of China already gave a speech entitled 'Go to the Countryside,' which deeply hit the mark. The Shanghai Banking Association also established a Rural Finance Adjustment Committee. The Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank has independently focused on rural loans, diligently experimenting and achieving considerable results. However, the effectiveness has not yet been widespread, and it is not helping the entire countryside. Why is this? It is because there is no large-scale joint organization of official, commercial, and banking entities to provide joint relief. It is now proposed that the Central Bank allocate funds to promote this, and that all commercial banks rise up and catch up to jointly address this critical situation. The revival of the countryside can then be hoped for. Some say that the Central Bank is not a direct business operation. This is indeed the case. However, they do not know that agriculture is the foundation of the country. If the countryside goes bankrupt, how can the nation stand? Rising up to rescue it is an inescapable duty. Moreover, this involves allocating funds for rural lending, not the bank itself directly engaging in business operations. This is the meaning stipulated in Articles 1, 2, and 3 of this outline. Some say that commercial banks are not charitable organizations, and cannot recklessly throw the shareholders' capital and depositors' money into poor and remote areas, where it would be easy to lend but difficult to recover. This is also indeed the case. However, loans must have secure collateral and guarantees, so the concerns should be allayed. This is the meaning stipulated in Articles 5 and 6 of this outline. In summary, if this proposal is not implemented, even if hundreds of millions of dollars are raised annually for passive relief, it will ultimately be of no avail. Furthermore, with all industries in decline, and merchants and the people in distress, fundraising has already reached its limit. Gentlemen in the banking community, with true insight and foresight, have acted early. They will surely express their sympathy. Therefore, this outline is specially drafted and respectfully submitted for public decision."

Loan Outline 144

(1) It is proposed that the official and commercial banks in Shanghai jointly organize a loan to the countryside, to be named the Shanghai Banking Community Rural Loan Group. (2) It is proposed that the official and commercial banks in Shanghai temporarily allocate 10 million national currency as the Rural Loan Group's fund. If necessary, the banking group will decide to increase it. (3) For the allocation of funds in the previous article, it is proposed that the Central Bank undertake 30%, and the remainder be undertaken by the member banks of the Banking Association in proportion to the amount of their share capital. (4) The General Group will establish a General Management Office in Shanghai. Branches, sub-branches, or agencies will be established in various provinces, cities, counties, and towns as appropriate. Their organization will be determined by the banking group. (5) The sole purpose of the Loan Group is to promote production and revitalize the countryside. Its business is as follows: (A) Accepting commissions from the countryside to handle the transportation and sales of agricultural products, and the purchase of agricultural implements, livestock, seeds, and fertilizers. (B) Addressing the needs of the countryside by providing loans secured by agricultural products, agricultural implements, livestock, clothing, jewelry, etc., and issuing loans guaranteed by designated agricultural products (including unfinished products such as sericulture). (C) Negotiating with local governments regarding loans for rural water conservancy projects. (D) Negotiating with rural cooperatives for credit loans. For all the above items, the branches, sub-branches, or agencies must investigate and complete forms, and submit them to the General Management Office for approval before proceeding. Detailed procedures will be separately formulated by the General Office. (6) The rural organizations responsible for guaranteeing interest payments or repayment to this office are as follows: (A) Provincial or (municipal) government, (B) County government, (C) Rural cooperatives, (D) Respected gentry and merchants in the area. (7) The local government in the location where the General Office, branches, sub-branches, or agencies are located is responsible for protecting their safety. (8) After this outline is resolved by this association, it will be recommended to the banking community for consideration and implementation.

Red Swastika Society Reports the Tragic Situation in the Disaster Area of Jiangxi Province 146

Rats are bigger than cats… Mosquitoes and fleas jump around.

The Red Swastika Society's relief teams, Teams One and Two, have arrived in Jiangxi one after the other, and all the relief supplies have also been continuously transported there. It is reported that the General Office of the Society in Shanghai received a report yesterday from Zhou Zongliang, the head of the team, regarding the tragic situation in the disaster area, which is unbearable to witness. Excerpts are as follows: (Omitted above) Zongliang departed from the provincial capital on the morning of December 28th, accompanied by Team Leaders Han and Li, Team Captain Nie, Team Member Peng, Doctor Wen Chi, and eleven servants, traveling by car along the highway. That afternoon, they arrived in Nancheng, and at 5:00 PM, they arrived in Nanfeng, staying at Dechanghao, managed by Qian He. They met with County Magistrate Liu and Police Officer Mei, and learned that the Kutou area of the county was still unsettled and being suppressed. There were about 3,000 refugees who were homeless. This morning, they departed for Guangchang, which was a newly recovered area in June of the 23rd year. The area was lost and regained three times, resulting in the most deaths and injuries. Although the corpses were buried by the army, they were all covered with loose soil. Without heavy work, the epidemic could not be eliminated. Those who survived were all elderly, weak, disabled, hungry, and cold. Their faces were colorless. The disaster victims mostly suffered from malaria, dysentery, and beriberi. In the entire county, there were no strong men or women. This tragic situation could not be believed without witnessing it firsthand. On the way, they encountered a disaster victim holding a bowl of rice, lying on the side of the road, barely breathing, still struggling to get up. They were planning to find a way to save him, but before they could, he died. That evening, they stayed at the Pingmin Grand Hotel, whose buildings were all piled up with mud, and the stench was overwhelming, making them want to vomit. County Magistrate Hui and the chairman of the Chamber of Commerce came to meet them. According to them, a month ago, dozens of people were found dead on the road every day, so seeing one person was not unusual. It can be seen that the lives of the disaster victims in the county were hanging by a thread. Without urgent relief, they would not be able to survive. County Magistrate Hui was very happy to hear that the association had brought clothing, rice, food, medical supplies, doctors, etc. He also asked if there were any rat poison because after the disaster, the rats were larger than cats and were a nuisance everywhere, impossible to catch. The disaster victims compared them to large insects. Even more strange was that in the severe winter weather, there were still mosquitoes and flies rampant. The team could not sleep peacefully, and the rats were even more vicious. In addition to mosquitoes and rats, there were also soil fleas jumping around. These mosquitoes and fleas sucked human blood and could be a medium for malaria. Therefore, medical work is currently critical, but the fundamental way to reduce the epidemic is to kill rats and mosquitoes. It is not considered successful without doing so. They originally planned to go directly to Ningdu, but that night, it rained heavily. Guangchang to Ningdu was only 120 li, but the roads were all made of piled-up mud and had to pass over 18 li of mountain ridges. Heavy vehicles could not travel. It was heard that military vehicles had already overturned. They had no choice but to return to the province. The next morning, they departed from the province. The rain had not stopped. After the car passed Nancheng, although the road was very flat, the mud was soaked with rainwater, and the stones were exposed. While driving, the car suddenly swerved and slid to the side of the pond, only half a foot away from the pond water. Fortunately, the engine was stopped, avoiding an accident. Along the way, there were no signs of human habitation. In the rain and snow, they took more than a dozen photos of the disaster area. After they are developed, they will bring them back. They passed through a village with very large houses, right next to the road, but there was no one there. In the hall, there was a corpse, only the clothes and bones were visible. Upon repeated examination, it was about one or two years old. No one knew who the family was. Everywhere, there were remains and skeletons. In addition, this year there were droughts and floods, and the fields were barren. The severity of the disaster was unparalleled. On the 29th, they stayed in Fuzhou, and on the 31st, they returned to the province safely. An investigation revealed that there were more than 60 counties in the disaster area of Jiangxi. The counties in southern and eastern Jiangxi had been devastated and were also hit by drought, resulting in an extremely tragic disaster situation. They planned to first select the two counties of Guangchang and Ningdu, located in southern Jiangxi near Fujian, to handle first. They had already dispatched Teams One and Two, one after the other, to Guangchang and Ningdu. However, the disaster area is vast and there are many disaster victims. They deeply hope that the gentlemen in Shanghai who live in luxurious houses and have ample food and clothing will take a look at the disaster area and understand the misery of human hell.

Municipal Zoo

Purchasing Seven Major Animals 147

Expanding the Park Area and Building Lion and Elephant Houses

Will Purchase Zebras, Seals, and Seven Other Animals

Since the establishment of the Municipal Zoo more than a year ago, the zoo has been working hard to expand its facilities. The zoo has recently been approved by the municipal government for this year's expansion plan, which includes purchasing various new animals. The details of the plan are excerpted as follows:

Purchasing Novel Animals 148

The zoo currently only has large animals such as lions, tigers, leopards, wolves, bears, elephants, camels, and sika deer. For the purpose of expansion, the zoo has specifically requested and been approved by the municipal government to purchase seven major animals in the first half of this year, including zebras, rhinoceroses, polar bears, seals, chimpanzees, ostriches, and giraffes. Director Shen of the zoo has already studied the purchase and transportation process, and will submit a request to the municipal government for funds to implement the plan to purchase novel animals. It is expected that they will be transported to Shanghai in the first half of this year for public viewing.

Commencing Construction of Animal Houses 149

The current area occupied by the zoo is only a little over seven mu. Recently, though, an additional seven fen of neighboring land has been purchased nearby, but it is still not sufficient. As a result, the elephant and camel houses are temporarily constructed with wooden planks and reed sheds, which is not suitable for the animals' living conditions. The newly purchased land will be used to build houses for elephants and camels. In the future, zebras, chimpanzees, and other animals can also be housed there. The designs for the houses have been completed, and construction is scheduled to begin this spring. Once construction is completed, other animals such as wolves, monkeys, wild boars, etc., will also be moved into the new houses.

Heating Equipment Installed 150

The zoo's animals, such as snakes and crocodiles, are all tropical species, and some are hibernating animals. In view of this cold winter weather, the zoo specifically requested and was approved by the municipal government to replace the original water radiators, which were not suitable for tropical and hibernating animals, with heating equipment by the Bureau of Public Works. The installation was completed yesterday. The heating can maintain a temperature of 40 degrees Fahrenheit, so even if it is snowing heavily outside, the internal temperature can be maintained above 60 degrees.

Muslims in the City

Observing the Eid al-Fitr Ritual This Morning 151

According to the Guowen News Agency, Muslims in the city must fast for one month every year during the ninth month of the Islamic calendar. The intention is to restrain food and lust in order to be careful about desires. Every year, according to the calculation of the Kaaba, the Earth revolves around the Sun for 365 and a quarter days, which is called a year. The moon becomes full twelve times, which is 354 and a third days, which is called a year. A year is used to calculate human affairs, all ceremonies should follow 12 months, the ninth month of every year is the month of fasting. During this month, diet should be restricted and sexual activity completely abstained. This is meant to be an exercise in restraint and desire. Before the fast, there must be a determination. Without a sincere determination, there will be no success. With an improper determination, the success will be distorted. Each virtuous act must start with an intention. So, Muslims during this month must eat before dawn and only break the fast after sunset. There is one month of fasting, one month is thirty days, one month is twenty-nine days, observing the lunar cycle. One must wait until dawn, after breaking the fast, to compensate the fast. Today (7th), Muslim followers have reached the end of fasting, each must shower, wear perfume, and put on clean clothes, pay "Saudak" (a form of alms giving), those with savings of more than forty silver dollars must give one dollar to charity, the charity will be distributed to relatives (excluding parents, grandparents, children), neighbours, countrymen, distribute according to amount, or subsidise cultural activities, no sending alms to distant places, but distant relatives are accepted. Recite praises, each follower is to gather at the Zhejiang Road Mosque, Fuyou Road Mosque, Xiaotaoyuan Mosque, Xiaoshadu Mosque, Xieqiao Mosque, Xiaonanmen Mosque, and at more than ten other mosques to hold a big ceremony. The missionary will give a lecture on teachings and welcome attendees to visit.

Published by the French Municipal Council

Last Year's Injury and Death Statistics 152

According to statistics released by the French Concession Municipal Council, the number of traffic accidents in the French Concession last year increased by more than 40% compared to the previous year. There were 2,921 cases last year, compared to 2,081 cases in 1933. Fortunately, the number of deaths decreased, with 33 deaths last year, compared to 35 deaths in 1933. Measures Stipulated by the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company

Preferential Treatment for Student Travel 153

Group Travel on Single or Round Trips with Price Reductions

Must Have School Principal's Certificate to Enjoy Preferential Treatment

The state-owned China Merchants Steam Navigation Company was instructed by the Ministry of Transportation to encourage schools to organize tour groups to visit factories or schools in various places to promote the effectiveness of education. The company has formulated the following preferential measures, which are detailed below.

Request from the Ministry of Education 154

The suggestion for the preferential treatment measures was jointly submitted by six colleges, including National Peiping University, Peiping Wuhan University, and Peiping Institute of Technology, to the Ministry of Education. In order to encourage education and provide preferential treatment for student travel, they specifically requested that the Ministry forward their request to the Ministry of Transportation and the Ministry of Railways to provide free preferential treatment in accordance with the practice of Jiaotong University. After receiving the request, the Ministry of Education forwarded it to the two ministries for review and implementation. However, the Ministry of Railways stated that it was restricted by its regulations and could not comply. The Ministry of Transportation instructed the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to properly formulate measures for implementation.

Preferential Measures 155

A reporter from China Press inquired with the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company yesterday and learned that the company had formulated several principles for the preferential treatment measures. For example, if there are more than ten students traveling together, a single trip ticket can be reduced by 25% from the regular passenger ticket price, and a round-trip ticket can be reduced by 50% from the regular passenger ticket price. However, it is stipulated that the school principal must formally issue a letter of certification, sign and seal it, and add the school's official seal, detailing the number of people and the starting and ending points. Prior notice must also be given in advance in order to enjoy the preferential treatment measures according to the above regulations.

Second Chicken Contest Results 157

The Zhuangqiao Farmers' Education Center in Shanghai County held its second chicken contest a few days ago. Director Zhang Zhou Shilin, Lu Zongda, Ru Xiaojiang, and others served as judges. The judges scored on three criteria: (1) weight, (2) conformation, and (3) plumage. The results were: first place for male chicken went to Zhou Xianghe, second place to Zou Shulin, third place to Kang Tongsheng, fourth place to Huang Jingzhou, fifth place to Shi Mengliang, and sixth place to Zou Maosheng. For female chickens, first place went to Zou Hansheng, second place to Zou Lumin, third place to Zhou Baisen, fourth place to Zhou Shusheng, fifth place to Kang Hesheng, and sixth place to Kang Yujiang. The Farmers' Education Center awarded prizes to all winners to encourage them.

Jian Hao Sentenced to Six Months for Assault 158

Jian Hao, a Guangdong native, snuck into the Hongkou small vegetable market at 5:40 AM. He tried to steal beef from the stall of Tang Liansheng, a Pudong native, but failed, leading to an argument. Jian, enraged, grabbed a sharp knife from a neighboring beef stall and stabbed Tang in the right arm. Tang fell to the ground and cried for help. Patrolman No. 1088 arrived after hearing the commotion and arrested Jian, taking him and the knife to the Hongkou Police Station. The arrest was reported to the police chief, who ordered Jian's detention. The injured Tang was taken to Tongren Hospital for treatment. Fortunately, the injury was minor, and he was discharged after being bandaged. The next morning, Jian was sent to the First Special District Court. Lawyer Li Zhishan of the Public Works Department presented the facts and the weapon and requested prosecution. Tang Liansheng testified about what happened. When questioned, the defendant stammered. Judge Jiang reviewed the evidence and sentenced Jian Hao to six months of imprisonment as a warning.

Zhabei Soup Kitchen Suddenly Closed 159

Refugee Numbers Surge, Capacity Insufficient

Shouting and Noise Could Easily Cause Trouble

Currently Negotiating to Open Another Soup Kitchen

Reason for Closure Reported to the Social Affairs Bureau

The Zhabei Charity Association opened the second soup kitchen on Liuying Road on the morning of January 1st at 6:00 AM. Reports of the extraordinary crowding of soup drinkers have been documented in the press. The association reports that the number of refugees has been increasing daily, making the second Liuying Road facility unable to accommodate them. The resulting shouting and noise have led to a tense situation, forcing the association to temporarily close the kitchen the previous morning. The situation is described below:

Number of Soup-Drinking Poor Explodes 160

When the association opened the soup kitchen on the morning of January 1st, it initially distributed six dan of rice, cooked into ten cauldrons of soup. However, the number of refugees reached over 3,000, making the supply insufficient. The association's director, Wang Binyan, distributed nine copper coins to each person after the soup ran out to resolve the situation. The next day, the association increased the rice supply to eighteen dan, believing it would meet the demand. However, the number of refugees increased to over 12,000, and there was still not enough soup for everyone. The association once again resorted to distributing copper coins.

Sudden Announcement of Closure 161

For months, the number of refugees has continued to increase, making the second Liuying Road facility unable to accommodate them. Even with an increase to twenty-six dan of rice, there were still those who missed out, leading to shouting and noise and a very tense situation. Therefore, the association had no choice but to announce the temporary closure of the soup kitchen starting the morning before yesterday, fearing that the refugees might use the situation to cause trouble. The Shanghai North Security Corps sent a team to maintain order. However, some elderly refugees were still given copper coins. The refugees reluctantly dispersed by 10:00 AM, and fortunately, no incidents occurred.

Post-Closure Negotiations Underway 162

Although the soup kitchen has closed, the refugees are hungry and unable to eat. Yesterday morning, before 5:00 AM, many people gathered outside the Liuying Road soup kitchen. The association sent people in advance to the entrance to explain the situation to the refugees, who gradually dispersed. The scene was quite tragic. A reporter from the Datong News Agency then went to the association's headquarters on Datong Road to inquire about the post-closure arrangements. According to the staff, Director Wang Binyan has visited Wang Yiting, the chairman of the Shanghai Charity Organization Federation, to discuss solutions and plans to open another soup kitchen nearby to provide relief and prevent trouble. The association has also reported the reason for the closure to the Social Affairs Bureau.

Five Trade Associations of Shanghai Tobacco and Alcohol Industry 164

Joint Meeting Held Yesterday 165

Due to the Financial Bureau's Increase in Spring License Fees

A Joint Petition will be Submitted to Request a Temporary Delay in the Increase

The five trade associations of the Shanghai tobacco and alcohol industry recently held a joint meeting on the afternoon of 4:30 PM because the Financial Bureau had begun collecting spring tobacco and alcohol license fees and had increased the amount, which was difficult to bear. Representatives from the tobacco exchange, including Chen Liangyu, Chen Ruilin, Qian Wenda, Zhang Songji, and Mi Chuxin; tobacco and alcohol industry representatives Xie Zhendong and Zeng Tangshen; local yellow wine industry representative Fang Zhongheng; sauce and preserves industry representatives Chen Weiwen and Zhang Dalian; and Shaoxing wine industry representative Zhang Qingfang attended the meeting. Chen Liangyu was elected chairman, and Zhang Jinzhi was the recorder. After formalities, the chairman reported the purpose of the meeting. Zhang Song reported that the collection of spring tobacco and alcohol licenses had begun and that the tobacco industry had reported an increased burden due to investigator reports. The association convened the joint meeting to discuss relief measures. Zhang Dalian, the representative of the sauce and wine industry, reported on the license acquisition process for each member. After detailed discussion, the representatives agreed that the members of each industry were experiencing poor business and were already unable to bear the winter tobacco and alcohol licenses. If the fees were increased again, it would be impossible for the industries to pay. To protect the interests of the industries, it was unanimously decided that the chairman would lead a joint petition from the associations to the Financial Bureau to maintain the status quo to show consideration for the difficulties of businesses. The meeting adjourned at 5:00 PM.

Young Woman Throws Infant from Window in a Fit of Madness, Killing the Child 168

Jiang Yuan Lost Her Mind

Suddenly Sends Her Son to His Death

Jiang Jinkui, from Suzhou, runs a bamboo chopstick shop at No. 21 Xinjie, Xuejia浜 Road, outside Xiaonanmen in Nanshi. He is married to Yuan, 39 years old, and they have had four children. Their eldest son, Fugeng, was unfortunately abducted by bandits at the age of eight and has never been found. The second child was a daughter who died of illness last year. Therefore, only two young children remain: Fuyuan, six years old, and Asi, only two months old. However, Yuan has a history of mental illness that comes and goes. The family is poor and lacks the resources to cure the root of the illness. Unexpectedly, at around 5:00 PM the day before yesterday, Yuan's old illness relapsed. She suddenly started waving her hands and feet, crying and laughing incoherently. Her family did not pay much attention. Soon, Yuan grabbed her lively and adorable young son, Asi, from the bed, opened the window, and threw him straight onto the street from the front of the building. As a result, the child's head hit a stone on the street, shattering it instantly, and his brains splattered out. He cried out in agony and died. At the time, Yuan was standing upstairs, witnessing her beloved son's tragic death. Instead of crying in pain, she laughed out loud. The local police heard about the incident and rushed to the scene. They immediately took Yuan to the Dongjiadu Police Station under their jurisdiction. During the preliminary interrogation by the station chief, Yuan's answers were not relevant to the questions. Because the incident involved causing death by negligence, the police prepared a document the next morning and sent it to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for questioning. However, if Yuan was indeed suffering from a mental illness, then, according to the criminal law's provision that actions of those who have lost their minds are not punishable, it is different from manslaughter by negligence. However, according to the law, considering the circumstances, she may be subject to imprisonment.

Bandit Commits Suicide in Detention Out of Fear of Punishment 169

Bao Shuji, a Chinese detective at the Hongkou Police Station, along with Western detectives, arrested five bandits from Jiangbei, including Wang Zhongde, Wu Qingcai, Qin Chunlian, Gu Baoyin, and Liu Xiaowuzi, at teahouses and Maigen Road at No. 43, Lane 460, Aven Avenue on the afternoon of the 2nd of this month. Two Mauser pistols and nine bullets were found on Wang and Wu. They were taken to the police station and detained. The day before yesterday, they were sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Lawyer Li Zhishan of the Public Works Department stated that the defendants were related to the armed robbery of the Mao Jinji Watch Shop at No. 29 Pan Road at 7:40 PM on December 25th of last year. Wang and Wu each had a watch and three pawn tickets. He requested a postponement for detailed investigation. The guns, bullets, and evidence were presented for inspection. Han Xianyi, an apprentice at the shop, testified that fifty-five watches and three gold rings were robbed at the time and identified Wang Zhongde and Wu Qingcai as the robbers. Wang held a Mauser pistol and threatened them into silence, also stealing watches. When questioned, Wang Zhongde stammered. Wu Qingcai admitted to going to the robbery with Wang and that the watch was indeed stolen. Qin, Gu, and Liu denied the charges. Judge Xiao ordered them to be remanded in custody for further investigation. Wang, who was 36 years old, tore his clothes into strips in the detention center of the police station at around 2:00 AM yesterday morning and hanged himself on the gate out of fear of punishment. Officer No. 504 discovered the suicide and informed the police chief, who ordered him to be sent to the police hospital for emergency treatment, but he was already dead. The body was transported to the autopsy center on Fielun Road. Prosecutor Tang from the court arrived at the center and confirmed that Wang Zhongde, a male, had committed suicide by hanging. Since no family members could be found, the body was handed over to the Pushan Villa for burial.

Property Dispute at the Samsung Stage 170

Pang Laichen and Others Counter-Sue Qiu Zijia and Others

Zhou Bingchen, Zhao Ruquan, and the deceased Huang Chujiu jointly founded the Samsung Business Company, leasing land from Pang Laichen on Niuzhuang Road to build the Samsung Stage Theater and market houses for rent. Later, Huang passed away, and Zhou and Zhao developed ill feelings. The company's assets were incorporated into Zhou's. Last fall, due to business failure and mounting debts, including tens of thousands of dollars in unpaid rent, Zhou sold the theater and market houses to Pang for $270,000. Not long after the transaction, Qiu Zijia and other creditors of the Gongfa Company, founded by Huang Chujiu, heard about it. They argued that since Huang was one of the shareholders of Samsung, the assets of Samsung should be jointly owned by Huang and could not be disposed of by Zhou alone. They hired lawyer Dong Yu to submit a petition to the Second Special District Court, which was forwarded to the First Special District Court, requesting the sealing of the property and instructing all tenants to deposit rent payments with the court on a regular basis pending review of the disposition. This decision was greatly disadvantageous to Pang Laichen, who then hired lawyer Qin Liankui to file a lawsuit against Qiu Zijia and others, raising an objection to the enforcement. First, the suit stated that the Samsung Company leased land from him to build the houses and that he had filed a lawsuit in court to force Zhou Bingchen to pay the rent owed. It described how Zhou took over the original leased property in September and paid to buy the buildings on the land because he was heavily in debt and unable to support himself. Then, the suit argued the legal principles in detail, stating that Qiu and others had no right to request enforcement because Huang Chujiu's shares had already been incorporated into Zhou's, so the defendants had no right to enforce the Samsung property. Finally, the suit requested a judgment: (1) the property in dispute should not be subject to enforcement for Huang Chujiu's debts; (2) the defendant's request for enforcement should be deemed an infringement and they should be held liable for damages; and (3) the defendants should bear the costs of the litigation. On the afternoon of the day before yesterday, Judge Peng Shi of the First Special Court held a hearing. After the plaintiff's lawyer stated the reasons for the lawsuit and presented the written evidence, requesting review, the defendant's lawyer also made a rebuttal. Judge Peng ruled that further investigation was needed and adjourned the hearing.

Appeal of Russian Murderer Rejected 171

Russian Pi Anjin Xia Gufu (transliteration, 29 years old) was a soldier under Zhang Zongchang of the Feng Army and had a feud with his platoon leader, La Fulao Fu Ni Gula (transliteration, 34 years old), who was of the same race. After disbandment, Pi came to Shanghai to seek a living, while La traveled to the three northeastern provinces, Harbin, Tianjin, Hankou, and other ports. He came to Shanghai at the end of October of last year. At around 10:00 PM on November 3rd, the two met in Lane 855 of Xiafei Road in the French Concession. Pi pulled out a sharp blade and stabbed La in the back three times before fleeing. La went to the Gongji Hospital for treatment and reported the incident. The French police arrested Pi and sent him to the Second Special Court. He was initially charged with assault and detained. La died of his injuries on the 13th of that month. The police changed the charge to premeditated murder and filed a public prosecution. The result of the trial was that Pi Anjin Xia Gufu was sentenced to twelve years of imprisonment and ten years of deprivation of civil rights. Pi did not accept the verdict and filed an appeal with the High Court's Third Branch. The High Court's panel of judges conducted a final hearing and determined that the appellant's appeal was without merit. Judge Guo, along with Associate Judges Sun and Fan and Prosecutor Zhang, opened a court session and ordered the appellant, Pi Anjin Xia Gufu, to be brought to court. The appeal was rejected. After the verdict, he was remanded to the detention center to await the third instance appeal period before being sent to prison for execution.

New Rickshaws in the Special District Began to Be Used Yesterday 172

A Total of One Hundred and Thirty-One Vehicles

Elegant, Lightweight, and Comfortable Design

The Public Rickshaw Management Committee of the Shanghai Public Concession decided to reform the structure and style of rickshaws. Replacement Begins 173

A total of one hundred and thirty-one new rickshaws were operating on the roads yesterday. Eighty-three of them were manufactured by Feixing Motor Vehicle Company. New Vehicle Style 174

National Goods Assistance Participation Regulations 177

The participation regulations for the National Goods Movement Profit-Sharing Assistance Conference, jointly initiated by the association and the All-Zhejiang Disaster Relief Association, are as follows:

(1) This conference is initiated by the All-Zhejiang Disaster Relief Association and the Chinese National Products Manufacturers Association and is named the Shanghai National Goods Movement Profit-Sharing Assistance Conference.

(2) The purpose of this conference is to utilize the National Goods Movement, implement profit-sharing assistance, promote production and sales cooperation, and provide relief to disaster victims.

(3) All national goods manufacturers who endorse the purpose of this conference may participate in accordance with the regulations.

(4) In addition to establishing an exhibition department, this conference will also establish a commercial venue and organize a commercial venue committee, appointing fifteen members. The commercial venue committee will establish a general affairs section, a public relations section, a design section, a publicity section, a venue affairs section, and a secretariat to handle all matters entrusted by the commercial venue committee.

(5) All manufacturers in the commercial venue group will allocate 2% of their business income to the assistance fund.

(6) The invoices used by manufacturers participating in the commercial venue group will be printed by the All-Zhejiang Disaster Relief Association in a prescribed three-part form, one for the customer, one for the All-Zhejiang Association, and one for the manufacturer. The assistance fund will be settled and extracted based on the invoices.

(7) The total amount of assistance funds raised will be reported in detail and publicly after the conclusion of this conference, and the All-Zhejiang Disaster Relief Association will be responsible for distributing the relief.

(8) The preparation costs of this conference will be borne equally by the participating manufacturers, as follows:

(1) For each booth in the commercial venue group, a fee of 45 yuan will be charged, plus a publicity fee of 5 yuan. This will be applied proportionally for multiple booths.

(2) For those participating in the exhibition department, a fee of 10 yuan will be charged for each type A exhibit and 5 yuan for each type B exhibit.

(9) Registration will begin immediately and will close five days before the opening of this conference. No extensions will be granted.

(10) Participating manufacturers must pay all fees in full at the time of registration to cover the conference's preparation expenses.

(11) This conference is scheduled to open on January 15th and will last for three weeks. If an extension is needed, a meeting of manufacturer representatives will be convened to decide.

(12) This conference will rent vacant land across from the Great World amusement park at the intersection of Min Ti Ni Yin Road and Ai Duo Ya Road to build a reed shed as the venue. (The preparation office is located at No. 4, Yongji Lane, Xizang Road, telephone 94185.)

(13) This conference will build 250 booths. The booths for each manufacturer will be determined by drawing lots.

(14) At the end of this conference, all participating manufacturers will be evaluated based on the quality of their products and the amount of profit-sharing they contributed. Certificates will be awarded by the conference to encourage them.

(15) Manufacturers participating in the commercial venue group must issue invoices for all goods sold. Their staff must follow the New Life Movement and obey the guidance of this conference. If there are any violations or other improper conduct, this conference may impose disciplinary actions.

(16) The lighting in all departments of this conference's venue will be provided by this conference. However, it is stipulated that each booth will be equipped with two 25-watt light bulbs. If manufacturers wish to add more lights or increase the wattage, the installation costs and electricity fees will be borne by the manufacturers themselves and must be reported to the venue affairs section of this conference for approval.

Violence by the Thirty-Six Gangs 178

Assault After Extortion Fails

In the city, the Nanshi district, and other areas of this city, there is a type of hooligan commonly known as the Thirty-Six Gangs. Whenever a new shop opens, a house is being built or demolished, or there is a wedding or funeral, these people must demand a cut. If they are not satisfied, they will cause trouble. Even those who run small stalls must pay a certain amount each month, or else they will forcibly buy goods or commit other evils. Because these gangs have many followers, people do not dare to argue with them. As a result, the bandits become more rampant. Yesterday morning, Pan Guizheng, who runs a fish stall on Ninghe Road in the city, was asked by these hooligans to pay a cut. Pan replied that business was slow, and his family's livelihood was already barely sufficient, politely refusing them. The hooligans harbored a grudge and left in anger. After Pan closed his stall, he was walking through the Xiaotaoyuan area when the gang rushed up to him, led by a man nicknamed "White-Eyed Monk," and demanded six yuan. Pan did not have the money to pay, so he was surrounded and beaten. The gang punched and kicked him. Pan cried for help. When the police arrived, the hooligans had already fled without a trace. Pan reported the incident to the police station under his jurisdiction, requesting an investigation. According to reports, these hooligans use a certain stove shop in the area as their headquarters and spend all day there, posing a threat to the area. It is hoped that the authorities will pay attention to this.

Zhou Caiqing Dies Tragically from Coal Poisoning 179

Zhou Caiqing, a Ningbo native who runs a noodle stall in the vegetable market at the racetrack, sleeps in a nearby bungalow at night. The night before last, he lit a coal briquette stove to keep warm because it was cold. However, the small room was filled with fumes overnight, causing him to be poisoned by coal. At 6:00 AM yesterday morning, Ye Yongxing, a peddler, discovered the situation and managed to break open the door. However, Zhou was already dead. He reported the incident to the Chengdu Road Police Station, which transported the body to the autopsy center to await a court-ordered investigation.
