Medical and Disease Prevention Institutions in Zhenjiang 253

— Xie Bingshi

Apart from a few special municipalities, Zhenjiang can be considered important in the country. Because Jiangsu Province is wealthy in the country. Since the provincial government moved to Zhenjiang, Zhenjiang has become the capital of Jiangsu Province.

The term "provincial capital" has been used for several years, and it is naturally more important for medicine and health. The current Chairman Chen is doing his best to promote hygiene, so everything has developed considerably. Although it is not as developed as Shanghai and Nanjing, it is much better than before.

Currently, the largest medical institution in Zhenjiang is the Jiangsu Provincial Hospital. Before the establishment of the provincial hospital, the Hygiene Section of the Public Security Bureau set up a free clinic. There were no public general hospitals or health institutions. The private ones are about the same as those in other places, with the same complete equipment. The oldest one is the Hongren Hospital, which has an affiliated nursing school, and the Rural Nursing School run by Zhenjiang County. Next is the Christian Hospital and the Women and Children's Hospital, which were closed due to financial difficulties.

Before the establishment of public and private medical institutions, only informal doctors opened clinics. At that time, the public did not know what medicine was. They always thought that the medical institutions were good and received a lot of support.

Since the establishment of the Provincial Hospital, the provincial capital has benefited a lot. Each county directly under the jurisdiction of Jiangsu Province has also established county hospitals. These county hospitals are under the control of the Provincial Hospital. The location of the Provincial Hospital is not suitable, so branch clinics and free maternity hospitals were established in the city. At that time, the maternal mortality rate was very high, and there were no trained midwives. Due to the urgent need for such talents, several classes of midwives were recruited and taught about disinfection methods and simple delivery methods. The authorities felt that these trained midwives were still not fully effective. Therefore, they began to establish the Jiangsu Provincial Midwifery School. Each county sent two students per class. After graduation, they were assigned to work in various counties.

Zhenjiang's disease prevention institutions only started this year. A health office was established, specializing in prevention work and some treatment, school hygiene, store hygiene, and inspection of slaughterhouses. Licenses were given before they could operate. There is also a chemical laboratory to help with inspections.

The Provincial Medical and Political College opened in October. Chairman Chen serves as the president concurrently. There are four departments inside: the Department of Health Administration, the Department of Medicine (that is, the medical department), the Department of Health Education, and the Department of Medical Research (that is, traditional Chinese medicine receiving further training in scientific principles). These personnel are the basic health team of Jiangsu Province in the future.

There is no organization in the provincial capital that promotes disease prevention and treatment in writing. Later, the Hongren Hospital sponsored the "Public Medicine and Health" weekly, which was attached to the newspaper. A total of twenty-five issues were published. At that time, Zhenjiang newspapers focused on literature and expanded the literature section, so the "Public Medicine and Health" weekly was discontinued. In short, the Zhenjiang press has not yet recognized the importance of health and cannot fulfill its duties. Now, there are no more such publications in Zhenjiang.

Zhenjiang's waterworks has a relatively long history. The water source for water intake seems to be too close to the riverbank, and it is often contaminated by unclean objects. The water storage tank is sixteen feet deep and has a very small area. Alum is used to help it settle. There are ten filter beds, using rapid sand filtration. As a result, the water is very clear, but who knows how many bacteria this clear water contains! There is no disinfection method or chemical laboratory in their factory to test the water, which is the most terrible thing. Water is what people drink every day and has a close relationship with the human body. So, we should pay attention to this invisible killing machine.

I have said a lot, but it is not systematic. Let's end here for now! The future health of Zhenjiang will develop, and I will contribute more to readers later.

Chinese Medicine and Health in the Past Year (Part 1) 254

— Jiang Haiming

Introduction | Medical Education | Medical Group Activities | Medical Disputes | Medical Publishing | Medical Research | Medical Construction | Military Medical Training | A Glimpse of the Old Medical World | Trends in the New Pharmaceutical Industry | Survey of Rural Hygiene | Views on Urban Hygiene | Conclusion

(1) Introduction

The endless waves of time flow, never stopping, surging forward, and a year's time passes like a white horse flashing past a crack. We who talk about medicine must deeply reflect on the changes in Chinese medicine and health in the past year on the long historical stage, and make a whole and comprehensive description.

Chinese medicine and health in our country has a history of a hundred years since the introduction of Western scientific medicine. However, its hesitation and the stagnation of old medicine are both weaknesses of Chinese medicine and health in the past, which cannot compete with other countries in the world. Face reality and look forward to the future. We must also list and compare in detail the extent of progress in Chinese medicine and health in the past year as a way to improve.

This article is written from a historical perspective and describes the main points; it also evaluates its gains and losses with an objective eye. So that we can understand its outline, know its general trend, and consider how we should promote the advancement of Chinese medicine in the future? How to eliminate medical disputes in China? How to build a health cause in China? How to awaken the illusions of old medicine? How can Chinese medicine shine in the world? Although, this is not something that my humble pen can describe in its entirety. I only seek to offer a small contribution as a way to attract greater contributions, and I hope to gain the corrections and efforts of contemporary sages.

(2) Medical Education

What is the state of medical education in our country? Recently, Mr. Wang Qizhang of this publication has made a detailed evaluation, like a bright light in a dark room, illuminating everything! To sum up in one sentence, medical education in our country in the past was all passive and alienated education, and there are signs of a trend towards danger and death! In the twenty-third year, although the Ministry of Education established a Medical Education Committee and formulated an outline of curriculum standards, the tendency of medical education to become alienated has not decreased as a result. According to the survey, there are currently thirty-one medical schools in our country, and their nature can be roughly divided into five categories:

National 　　　　　　　　　　 Four

Provincial 　　　　　　　　　　 Six

Private 　　　　　　　　　　 Eight

Church and Foreign Established 　　　　　 Eleven

Military Medical 　　　　　　　　　　 Two

Observing the above table, we know that the number of medical schools established by churches and foreigners accounts for one-third of the total number of medical schools in the country. In recent years, the Ministry of Education has stipulated the graduation year limit of medical schools, setting the graduation year for medical colleges at six years and the graduation year for medical specialty schools at four years. However, the current academic programs of medical schools vary, with some graduating in seven years, six years, five years, and four years. If this cannot be unified, and there is so much foreign education, how can the alienation of medical education be actively corrected and achieve the goal of automatic and autonomous medical education in our country?

In mid-October of the twenty-third year, we vaguely heard that the draft of the medical curriculum standards prepared by the Medical Education Committee of the Ministry of Education had been officially completed, and opinions were solicited from medical experts in major cities such as Peiping, Shanghai, and Hankou. This shows that the members of the Medical Education Committee of the Ministry of Education have an open mind and see the seriousness of this matter. However, we must say a word:

We already know that medical education in our country is increasingly alienated! How to reverse this tide? It depends on what the medical curriculum standards will be in the future, and then we can make a decision. I am ashamed that I have not been able to see the full text of the medical curriculum standards set by the Ministry of Education this time, so I dare not express my opinion rashly. According to rumors, it seems that in the curriculum standards, foreign languages will be graded for medical texts, with Chinese as the top, German and French as the bottom, and Japanese even lower. If this is true, the result of the future medical education tending to alienation will be even worse than today? The language of a country is just a man-made symbol; in short, it is a symbol. If we want to absorb foreign knowledge, it is certainly a shortcut to learn foreign languages, but we cannot force ourselves to learn a certain country's language as good. Today's scholars need to be familiar with the languages of all countries, and then they can hope to take the advantages of each country, integrate them, and make them the advantages of our country. Otherwise, if we focus on the pursuit of a certain country's language, we will inevitably forget our ancestors, force the advantages of a certain country's knowledge, and despise what our country does not have; force the convenience of a certain country's language, and ridicule our country's language as useless. If we continue to do this, will the future scientific medicine in China not be particularly Westernized? Can we still ask about the alienation of medical education in our country in the future? We have witnessed the danger of this tendency. It is certainly impossible to disregard English, and it is not necessary to focus on German and French. Different people have different views, so the medical language cannot be forcibly stipulated.

Everyone knows that our country lacks doctors. In the twenty-third year, the number of graduates from various medical schools and the population ratio of our country is about one in 250,000, which is still weak, and there is a great sigh of talent shortage! I will list the accurate number of graduates from medical schools that I have investigated to see a glimpse.

Shanghai Medical College 　　　 Thirteen people

Medical College of Peking University 　 Forty people

Hebei Provincial Medical College 　　 Fourteen people

Peking Union Medical College 　 Twenty-five people

Guangzhou Xia Ge Medical College 　 Fourteen people

Shanghai St. John's Medical School Seventeen people

Shanghai Aurora University Medical College 　 Eight people

Jinan Qilu Medical College 　 Fourteen people

Shanghai Southeast Medical College 　 One hundred and fifteen people

"Note" Those that have not been accurately investigated are not included.

Observing from the above table, I deeply feel that the academic system of medical education in our country is

is not uniform. The smallest number of graduates from the medical schools listed above is only eight, and the largest number exceeds one hundred. Only the number of graduates from Peking University Medical College is relatively close to the 50 students per class stipulated by the Ministry of Education, and the rest are quite different. We feel that today, our country lacks medical talents, so the increase in the number of medical school graduates each year should, at a minimum, follow the standards stipulated by the Ministry of Education. Otherwise, it will be so difficult to cultivate medical talents, and the hope of popularizing scientific medicine in China will never come.

The medical terms in our country are numerous, dazzling, and not unified. In the spring of the twenty-third year, the Ministry of Education had the organization of a Medical Terminology Review Committee, hiring Mr. Song Wusheng, Zhu Hengbi, Tao Chichun, Song Guobin and other gentlemen as members, which is worth recording.

Common Sense Questions and Answers about Diseases 255

— Cheng Hanzhang

(50) Hemorrhoids and Anal Fissures

(Question) What are hemorrhoids?

(Answer) Hemorrhoids are a disease in which the hemorrhoidal veins at the anus become nodularly dilated.

(Question) Why is it said in colloquial terms: "Nine out of ten people have hemorrhoids"? Is this true?

(Answer) Not necessarily true, because this sentence is nothing more than a description of too many people suffering from hemorrhoids.

(Question) What is the difference between internal hemorrhoids and external hemorrhoids?

(Answer) All hemorrhoids located outside the boundary of the anal sphincter are external hemorrhoids; those located inside the boundary of the sphincter are called internal hemorrhoids.

(Question) What are the causes of hemorrhoids?

(Answer) The biggest cause is constipation, other such as rectal cancer, enlarged prostate gland, uterine tumors, pregnancy, sitting

Page 16

workers, chronic heart disease, and respiratory diseases, or cirrhosis of the liver, etc.

(Question) What symptoms occur after suffering from hemorrhoids?

(Answer) Most of the time, there is an unpleasant feeling in the anus during constipation or exercise, a feeling of tension, itching and pain, etc. There is bleeding. There is often persistent bleeding that leads to anemia, and there is also a feeling of tenesmus and burning.

(Question) What symptoms will occur if you suffer from hemorrhoids for a long time?

(Answer) Rectitis, rectal prolapse, eczema, etc. will occur. In severe cases, ulcers will also occur.

(Question) What should be done to prevent it?

(Answer) It is necessary to avoid constipation, have a bowel movement every day, give non-irritating foods, and prohibit drinking and smoking.

(Question) How to treat hemorrhoids?

(Answer) The treatment of hemorrhoids depends on the condition of external hemorrhoids and internal hemorrhoids.

(Question) How to treat external hemorrhoids?

(Answer) For external hemorrhoids, borax ointment can be applied with a bandage, or Orthoform ointment can be applied.

(Question) What about internal hemorrhoids?

(Answer) For internal hemorrhoids, borax ointment suppositories and cocaine hydrochloride cotton suppositories are used.

(Question) What should be done when bleeding occurs?

(Answer) Apply epinephrine solution or cotton swabs or perform surgical ligation, cauterization, etc.

(Question) What should be done when rectal prolapse occurs?

(Answer) Surgical reduction, boric acid warm wet compresses or surgical excision and suturing can be performed.

(Question) What is an anal fissure?

(Answer) This is an anal mucosal injury or small wound or small ulcer.

(Question) How does it happen?

(Answer) It is caused by pruritus ani, pinworms or hemorrhoids, etc.

(Question) How should anal fissures be treated?

(Answer) Ichthammol ointment can be applied to anal fissures, or Mercurschrome solution can be applied, or silver nitrate sticks can be used for cauterization.

Common Sense of Hygiene for Ears, Nose, Throat, and Eyes (Reading) 256

— Tang Renjin

(30) Eye Hygiene

Although the eyes are small, once they get sick, the danger is often great. Just look at the pain of blind people to get a general idea. Therefore, we should not neglect the health of our eyes in normal times. Here, I will briefly list ten points of its hygiene. If you can practice them, it may not be without benefit.

(1) Getting up early and going to bed early is a general principle of hygiene, and it is also the key to nourishing the eyes. We know that people who often suffer from conjunctivitis (red eye) do not usually get up early and go to bed early.

(2) Do not use towels in public places to avoid the spread of trachoma.

(3) Strong light and flashing light are enough to damage the eyes and must be avoided. Therefore, when walking in the hot sun in summer or the white snow in winter, it is best to wear dark or yellow protective glasses to avoid the stimulation of strong light.

(4) It is not advisable to read books while riding in a car, because the fonts shake and damage eyesight.

(5) If dust, sand, or coal ash gets into the eyes, do not rub the eyelids immediately. You should close your eyes for a while and wait for the foreign objects to flow out of the eyes with tears. Because tears can make the dust, sand, and coal ash attached to the eyes lubricate and flow out. That is, tears have the natural function of removing foreign objects from the eyes.

(6) The distance between the eyeball and the object being viewed should be 30 centimeters. The time spent reading and writing should not be too long. You should close your eyes often to rest and adjust the eye muscles, and do not let them work excessively.

(7) It is not advisable to read or write in places with insufficient light, direct sunlight, etc., or at dusk.

(8) The light for reading and writing must come from the front left above. Backlighting should not be used. The distance between the light and the object being viewed should not be too far or too close. About one and a half feet is the most appropriate. The light power should be 50 candle power. The lampshade should be green. The bulb should be frosted.

(9) Bowel movements must be smooth every day to avoid congestion in the eyes.

(10) Nearsighted eyes should wear appropriate corrective glasses. They should not be configured casually. They must be examined by an ophthalmologist and then configured by an optician to be appropriate.

A Brief Discussion of Pulmonary Tuberculosis 257

— Hu Jiayan

(5) Specialized Diagnosis | | Tuberculin Reaction

What are the methods of using tuberculin in diagnosis? It is divided into two types: eye reaction and skin reaction. On the skin reaction side, there are four different methods: skin scratch, skin application, intradermal, and subcutaneous. Adding the eye reaction, they are commonly known as the five tuberculin reactions. These five methods cover almost all applications in diagnosis. Regarding their detailed circumstances, I will now describe them one by one below...

(A) Eye Reaction: Use one drop of a 1% tuberculin solution and drop it into the conjunctiva of the eye. Usually, within eight to twenty-four hours, most tuberculosis patients will develop conjunctivitis in that eye. However, if the reaction is negative, one drop of a 4% solution can be dropped into the other eye to observe the final result. This diagnostic method is most suitable for suspected cases of tuberculosis with fever. However, it should be avoided in children who have had eye diseases, are currently suffering from eye diseases, or have glandular diseases.

(B) Skin Reaction: This is also known as the Pirquet test; the procedure is similar to the usual vaccination method. First, clean the skin of the upper arm or forearm with alcohol, then take one or two drops of tuberculin solution (a 25% solution mixed with 0.5% carbolic acid) and drop it onto the skin. Then, use a small knife to break the skin in that area; in addition, it is best not to create a wound at a considerable distance, so that the two sides can be compared accurately. If this reaction is positive, an inflammatory swelling will occur at the inoculation site; this situation is definitely not present in the other small skin wound. The reaction usually occurs between twenty-four and forty-eight hours; some occur rapidly within five or six hours, and some are delayed until three or four days later. Increased temperature is rarely seen. | | This method is the most widely used because there are no contraindications under any circumstances; and the value of its positive reaction is more accurate and reliable than that of the eye reaction.

(C) Cutaneous Reaction: Also known as the Moro ointment reaction. A pea-sized piece of ointment made of tuberculin and anhydrous lanolin is applied to the skin (preferably on the chest below the left clavicle) for about one or two minutes. The area of application should not be too large, about the size of a silver dollar. Usually, after twenty-four or forty-eight hours, reddish nodules will appear on the skin of the applied area, varying from a few to dozens; this is a manifestation of a positive reaction! This method has the same value as the skin reaction in tuberculosis diagnosis.

(D) Intradermal Reaction: What is called an intradermal reaction? It is the injection of tuberculin solution into the skin. At this time, a raised blister will usually appear on the skin surface, but it will gradually disappear. The initial concentration of the solution is about 1:5000, but it can later be increased to a concentration of 1:100 or 1:10. After twelve or twenty-four hours, if a positive reaction is found, a state of redness, swelling, and infiltration will occur at the injection site, and it will be painful. This situation is most severe at about forty-eight hours; the upper arm is the most obvious part, followed by the legs and abdomen. Systemic reactions, such as increased body temperature, are also extremely rare; therefore, there are no contraindications under any circumstances, and it is similar to the skin reaction. As for its diagnostic value, it is also very accurate; sometimes, when other methods have no results, this test is relied upon to determine the final outcome.

(E) Subcutaneous Injection Reaction: What is called a subcutaneous reaction? It is the injection of tuberculin solution using the usual subcutaneous injection procedure. This positive reaction mostly causes systemic symptoms, so this procedure must be performed with great care, and it is best to wait until all possible tests have not provided a satisfactory answer. When the patient receives the injection, the daily temperature and other symptoms must be clearly examined for three days in advance. If the usual temperature exceeds 37 degrees Celsius, it should not be injected. In addition, this test should be avoided if the patient has heart disease, kidney disease, or has recently coughed up blood. The concentration of the solution is usually a 1:1000 dilution. The initial dose only needs one-thousandth of the total diluted solution. If no positive reaction occurs, it can be gradually increased in increments, but it can only be increased up to ten times at most. Even if there is no positive reaction, it should be stopped at this point. After the patient is injected, they must rest in bed and not move, and the body temperature should be checked every two hours. The reaction is detected as early as seven or eight hours and as late as eleven or twelve hours. In addition to the local reaction, it also has both systemic and lesion symptoms, which the above four do not have.

An Overview of Malaria (3) 258

— Wang Xiaolan

Prognosis of Malaria

Tertian and quartan malaria rarely cause death. Only patients who are chronically ill, emaciated, or elderly and weak may develop heart and lung diseases, which are dangerous for the prognosis. The repeated attacks, gradual development into chronic malaria or malarial cachexia, are also the same. If a person with a strong physique contracts it, the reproduction of malaria parasites is often not vigorous, the attacks stop, and it seems to heal naturally. However, the asexual and sexual bodies of the parasites are still dormant in the body. When physical strength is weakened or other inducing factors occur, they take the opportunity to relapse. In winter, when the weather is cold, malaria is not transmitted, but it still occurs, which is actually due to this. According to Shigakiyo, there are cases of quartan malaria recurring after five to fifteen years. With proper treatment, malignant malaria is also easy to cure, but those who develop malarial cachexia or atypical symptoms often die. According to historical statistics, the mortality rate of blackwater fever is about 5% to 16%.

Diagnosis of Malaria

The characteristics of malaria are typical cold and fever attacks, splenomegaly, anemia, malaria parasites in the blood, and an increase in large mononuclear white blood cells. If blood is not examined and only other symptoms are used as diagnostic criteria, it is easy to confuse tertian and quartan malaria during the initial attack, or when the fever type of malignant malaria is irregular, or when several types of malaria parasites are mixedly infected, with typhoid fever, sepsis, pneumonia, pulmonary tuberculosis, miliary tuberculosis, relapsing fever, influenza, acute endocarditis, and liver syphilis. Chronic malaria is similar to cystitis, pyelonephritis, tonsillitis, sinusitis, tooth inflammation, latent abscesses, and intestinal parasitic diseases. Malarial cachexia is similar to leukemia and liver cirrhosis. Atypical malignant malaria is often misdiagnosed as cholera, meningitis, stroke, uremia, and acute poisoning. Without careful differentiation, it cannot be determined.

There are two methods for examining blood. One is to take the patient's blood, prepare a specimen, and examine it under a microscope. If only motile pigment granules and small pieces of protoplasm are found in the red blood cells, it is called the unstained examination method. The other is to prepare a blood specimen, fix it with absolute alcohol, and stain it with Romanowsky's method (i.e., one part of 1% methylene blue aqueous solution and five parts of 0.1% eosin aqueous solution, mixed and stained for 20 minutes), or Giemsa's method (i.e., five drops of Giemsa's solution and five milliliters of distilled water, mixed and stained for 15 minutes), or Wood's method (i.e., staining twice with 0.1% eosin solution and 0.25% Azur II solution). In the stained examination method, the red blood cells are pale red, and the malaria parasites are blue.

If there are few malaria parasites in the blood and they are not easy to detect, Ross's staining method can be used. A thick drop of blood is smeared on a slide and allowed to dry. It is then immersed in an equal mixture of 2% formaldehyde and 1% acetic acid for about 3 minutes to dissolve the hemoglobin. It is washed with water, dried, and then stained with Giemsa's method. If malaria parasites are latent in the spleen, liver, bone marrow, muscles, and other organs that store blood, the malaria parasite provocation method must be used. Cold water can be poured on the spleen area, or it can be irradiated with sunlight and artificial sun lamps, or adrenaline, boiled milk, or peptone can be injected into the muscles, or Arsacetin can be injected subcutaneously to change blood circulation or cause organ contraction, driving the malaria parasites into the blood. The examination is performed again after several hours.

Treatment of Malaria

(1) Special Treatment: In ancient times, cinchona bark was used to treat malaria. When Pelletier et al. isolated its important component, quinine (Chinin), which can kill malaria parasites in free blood, it gained a reputation for its remarkable efficacy. However, it is not effective against parasites residing in internal organs and the crescent-shaped sexual forms of malignant malaria. People with different constitutions or pregnant women may experience side effects such as dizziness, vomiting, tinnitus, and stomach upset, as well as the risk of inducing blackwater fever and abortion, which are its weaknesses. Since Schulemann et al. developed plasmoquine, which can kill the sexual forms of malignant malaria and supplement what quinine cannot, the combination of cinchona bark and plasmoquine is especially effective in treating malaria. Recently, Mietzsch et al. developed atabrine, which has the same function as quinine but without side effects. People with special constitutions or pregnant women can use it without worry, making the treatment of malaria more complete.

The daily dosage of quinine hydrochloride or quinine sulfate is 0.9 to 1.2 grams. For tertian and quartan malaria, it is advisable to take one gram five hours before the attack, or divide it into five doses of 0.2 grams every two hours, all of which must be taken for three consecutive days. Then, take 0.5 grams per day for three consecutive weeks to achieve a radical cure. Alternatively, atabrine can be taken three times a day, 0.1 grams each time, for seven consecutive days. For malignant malaria, after taking atabrine according to the previous method, take plasmoquine 0.03 to 0.04 grams per day for three consecutive days, or take QuinoPlasmoquine alone three times a day, one tablet each time, for three consecutive weeks, which is very effective. For severe cases, quinine or QuinoPlasmoquine can be injected intramuscularly. The above dosages should be reduced appropriately for the elderly and children.

Quinine hydrochloride (Chininum hydrochloricum) or quinine sulfate (Chininum sulfuricun) has an extremely bitter taste. For internal use in children, tasteless products such as Euchinin or Aristochin are often used, but the dosage of the two must be increased by half compared with quinine hydrochloride. To avoid oral quinine, injection and enema methods can be used. In addition, internal administration of methylenblau, three○three (Peracrina), spirocid, stophan耳所, totaquina, malarcan, etc., or injection of Neosalvarsan, has considerable efficacy in treating malaria, especially the combination of arsenic and quinine. However, it is ultimately not as effective as the combination of plasmoquine and atabrine or quinine.

(2) Symptomatic Treatment: When the patient is shivering, warm their limbs with a hot compress or a hot water bag. If vomiting occurs, cocaine can be taken internally or injected. When fever occurs, use an ice pack on the head and take cool drinks made of hydrochloric acid or citric acid. When sweating, prevent colds. If excessive sweating occurs, opium preparations can be taken, or the skin can be wiped with alcohol, acetic acid, etc. For chronic malaria and malarial cachexia, pay attention to nutrition and use blood-tonifying and stomach-strengthening agents. For splenomegaly, electrical therapy, cold water perfusion, mercury ointment application, iodine injection, or splenectomy can be performed. For blackwater fever attacks, the patient must be kept absolutely quiet, cardiotonics should be injected, and calcium chloride should be taken internally or injected to stop hemolysis. Normal saline should be injected or given as an enema, and diuretics should be used to prevent renal tubule obstruction.

(3) Post-Illness Care: After malaria attacks stop, the blood must be repeatedly examined, and the malaria parasite provocation method should be used to allow the parasites dormant in the internal organs to enter the blood and continue treatment in order to achieve a radical cure. The residence should have fresh air and sufficient sunlight. The diet should consist of meat, beans, green vegetables, fresh fruits, milk, eggs, cod liver oil, etc., which are rich in calories and iron. To promote blood regeneration, appropriate exercise or warm baths should be taken, and iron and arsenic agents that stimulate hematopoietic function, such as 奥拍太純, 補爾神, 万利康 etc., should be injected, or chicken Cinchona Iron wine and liver preparations such as 利凡命 should be taken internally. If anemia is too severe, a blood transfusion should be performed with a blood type that is compatible. For chronic malaria and malarial cachexia, it is advisable to choose a mountainous area of 1,500 to 2,000 meters for changing places to recuperate to increase red blood cells.

Prevention of Malaria

Anyone living in a malaria-endemic area or traveling to that area should take antimalarial drugs to prevent infection. If quinine is used, 0.2 grams can be taken on the first day, and the dose can be doubled every other day, repeated continuously, or one tablet of chicken Cinchona bark plasmoquine can be taken every night until malaria no longer occurs in the area or four weeks after leaving the area, which is often effective. In addition, avoid mosquito bites. The residence should be chosen in a high and dry area, because malaria mosquitoes prefer to fly low, especially in high-rise buildings. Sunflowers, etc. can be planted in the courtyard to keep the soil dry and clean, making it difficult for mosquitoes to hide. Mosquito nets should be hung on the bed, and the windows should be fitted with screens. If mosquitoes enter the room, pyrethrum can be burned to drive them away. When going out, using veils, gloves, or applying fresh 稌椽 sweat to exposed parts of the body provides more comprehensive protection.

For public prevention of malaria, British physician Ross advocated eradicating malaria mosquitoes and eliminating their means of transmission. The emphasis is on the government setting up specialists to improve low-lying and humid land within the territory, filling ponds and marshes, and opening rivers for diversion to completely drain stagnant water so that mosquitoes cannot breed. Gutter ditches should be watered with kerosene and other things on time to kill their larvae. The United States and other countries have worked hardest on this, and towns in the Panama area have already achieved results. German physician Koch advocated eradicating malaria parasites in the blood of patients and eliminating the source of transmission. The emphasis is on the government implementing malaria physicians who are government officials, stipulating prevention and treatment methods, and enforcing them on the general public during the malaria outbreak season so that those suffering from malaria can be radically cured. Italy and other countries follow this the most, and it is also effective.

The Malaria Committee of the League of Nations, in view of the different socio-economic conditions of various countries and the different living conditions of the people, found that it was not easy to imitate the effective methods of other countries. Therefore, in 1928, it publicly announced antimalarial guidelines, differentiating between urgent and non-urgent matters, proceeding in an orderly manner, first emphasizing the treatment of malaria to reduce the source of infection, and then studying the types of malaria mosquitoes, habits, and breeding sites based on local conditions and environment, selecting appropriate prevention methods, and planning fundamental construction to improve social conditions and people's lives, so as to indirectly increase antimalarial capabilities. Finally, land improvement methods were implemented, drainage was carried out, and mosquitoes were eradicated to complete antimalarial work. Our people's lives are declining, and malaria is spreading more and more severely. The Ministry of Health has been implementing the national antimalarial guidelines step by step. If people across the country work together, we can complete it as early as possible. (The End)

Announcements 260

To Messrs. Ling Wenqin, Huang Kutong, Si Ren, Chen Yiru, Zhang Yifan, Ye Daguang, Zhu Wenqing: Your manuscript fees for December have been settled. Please collect them in person at the accounting department of this office from 2:00 PM to 4:00 PM daily, starting today until the 10th of this month.

Economic Supplement Editorial Department

Regarding a manuscript submitted to this publication under the pseudonym "Ying" entitled "The Causes of Price Drops": It has been with us for three to four months. Recently, due to year-end clearance of accumulated manuscripts, and because this publication values openness, believing that contributors expend brainpower and energy, we are happy to publish anything worthwhile. Thus, feeling this article still has some general reference value, we published it in issue No. 102 of this publication (23, 12, 24). We have now received a letter from Mr. Fang Caiying of the Economics Department of Nankai University in Tianjin, stating that the content of the article is identical to his article published in the 71st issue of the Tianjin Ta Kung Pao's Economic Weekly (July 11th), titled "The Seriousness and Causes of the Sharp Decline in Prices in China in Recent Years," which is blatant plagiarism. In addition to replying to Mr. Fang and canceling the payment as required, we originally intended to publish the name of the plagiarist. However, considering it might be a temporary impulse of material desire and ignorance of the shamefulness of plagiarism, we hope they can repent their past mistakes, make a serious effort, and improve daily. Who knows, someday they might become a writer. It depends on how the submitter under the pseudonym "Ying" conducts themselves from now on. Therefore, we will temporarily withhold their disclosure. Editor

Commercial News: Financial Call Loan Interest Reduced by Seven Points 261

The silver dollar market has largely cleared all year-end settlements, and with the bank holiday, the situation has become sluggish. Yesterday, the call loan interest rate for both morning and afternoon sessions was 4.8%, a decrease of seven points compared to the previous day. Transactions in call loan drafts amounted to over 2.4 million in the morning session for transfers, over 300,000 in new transactions, over 400,000 in the afternoon session, over 600,000 in transactions through the Small Exchange Association, over 900,000 in redemptions of silver pawn loans, over 800,000 in new loans, over 400,000 in remittances from various routes, and over 29.9 million in receipts and payments by private banks. Receipts and payments are at a standstill due to the bank holiday. The subsidiary currency market also showed weakness. In the morning session, Jiangnan small silver fell to 9 yuan, trading at 845 yuan. In the afternoon session, it slightly recovered by 3 yuan, changing to 848 yuan. As a result, it still fell by 6 yuan compared to the previous day. Transaction volume was 4,000 jiao in the morning session and 3,000 jiao in the afternoon session. Guangdong small silver was 759 yuan in the morning session, a decrease of 2 yuan compared to the previous day. Although it slightly recovered by a few jiao in the afternoon session to 759.6 jiao, the result was still a decrease of 1.4 yuan compared to the previous day. Transaction volume was 120,000 jiao in the morning session and 70,000 jiao in the afternoon session. Copper coins remained at 306,000 wen, the same as the previous day, with a transaction volume of 38,862 strings of cash, equivalent to 12,700 yuan in silver.

Securities: Government Bonds Faced Another Downturn Last Week 262

Trading Only Conducted for Two Days Due to New Year Holiday

Market Price Dropped by About 1.5 Yuan

Last week coincided with the end and beginning of the year. The end of the year was a market closure for brokers to settle accounts, and the beginning of the year was a three-day New Year holiday. Therefore, trading was only conducted for two days. During this long holiday period, although there was no significant progress or major obstacles in the political situation, the call loan interest rate rose to a new high of 6%, retreating only by 5 points during the relaxation. The tightness of the money market is undeniable. This is because the banking sector is completely tight, and depositors' withdrawals to purchase government bonds and for interest payment needs are extremely busy. The banking sector itself is solely engaged in speculation and has not changed its fixed policy of not speculating in government bonds. The previous rumor that HSBC Bank had shipped back 20 million yuan in cash from Hong Kong has not materialized. The Central Bank and the Bank of Communications prepared 10 million yuan for release, but only about 4 million yuan were actually transacted. Most transactions failed to materialize due to incompatible conditions. Therefore, borrowing is quite difficult. Considering the tightness of Shanghai's money market, there is no possibility of easing at present. However, the government is actively planning countermeasures. The market sentiment for government bonds is mostly bearish due to the above-mentioned factors. Short positions in the 16th issue are at least 7 to 8 million, and there are multiple others with short positions of 2 to 3 million. If there is a slight change in the money market, the rebound will be very rapid. Otherwise, there is a possibility of a further decline of 1 to 2 yuan. In terms of trends, the largest previous decline saw the 20-roll, 20-customs bonds fall below the 50 yuan mark, reaching 48 yuan and some change. The rebound then pushed above 50 yuan, with the 20-roll reaching above 51 yuan. This renewed downturn may break through the 50 yuan mark again, making it difficult to avoid seeing the previous low price again. However, it is necessary to be cautious about the implementation of government countermeasures. Last week, trading was only conducted on Friday, January 4th, and Saturday, January 5th. The call loan interest rate was 5.5% on both days. On Friday, the entire day trended downward due to selling by the Northern Consortium and the 21st issue, falling by 2 to 8 jiao compared to the year-end closing price of the previous year. On Saturday, the financial sector sold slightly, with issues 4 and 5 selling more. There were also unfounded rumors in the market, and the market price fell for three consecutive sessions. Although the closing price rebounded, it was only temporary short covering on the surface. Whether it has the ability to continue to rise depends on the level of call loan interest rates and whether the financial sector has buying interest as a prerequisite. As a result of last week's market prices, the decline ranged from 3 to 4 jiao to 1.2 to 3 yuan. The total transaction volume was 27,666,200 yuan.

Free Talk

Poets and Poetry 264

— Jiang Jiping

There is a section in the Suiyuan Shihua that discusses poets. It is very strange and very reasonable. It says, "Wang Xizhuang, Guanglu, wrote a preface for someone, saying, 'A poet is not necessarily someone who can write poetry. If one's mind is detached and one is gentle, even if one cannot read a single word, they are a true poet. If one's mind is petty and one is mundane, even if one spends all day poring over words and writing lengthy works, they are not a poet.'" This passage is very reasonable. One cannot become a poet casually, and it is especially difficult to become this kind of poet. Anyone can write poetry, but not everyone has talent. And so-called talent includes many elements, such as keen observation and rich emotion. If we were to discuss what constitutes keen observation, I am afraid we could not finish in a short time. Watching clouds is a very common thing, everyone can see them, but the clouds in the eyes of a poet are different from those in the eyes of an ordinary person. They can imagine many wonderful things from the clouds. The scene of snowfall is visible to everyone. Others only think that the sky is snowing and that everything in the universe is white, nothing more. But in the eyes of a poet, it is different. There are two lines of doggerel from the ancients that describe snowfall: "The river is a blur, the well mouth a black hole." It seems extremely ordinary, but in fact, it describes the snow scene very well. If we go to the countryside and go out to see it when it is snowing heavily, we will know the wonderfulness of these two lines of poetry. This is something that everyone can see, but others do not know that it can be used as poetic material. Good poems are often very ordinary, known to everyone, but not spoken by everyone. Everything in the world can be made into poetry. For example, the seller of hard sesame cakes at the door always shouts at night. Ordinary people hear it and do not feel much. But the poet hears it and can think that the seller of hard sesame cakes will one day not be able to do business. Thus, they imagine a child who buys hard sesame cakes every day, suddenly not hearing the seller of hard sesame cakes shout at the door one day. The child guesses that he may have died of old age, or that he was carelessly run over by a tram on the road, or that he was sick. Because the seller of hard sesame cakes once told the child that he was old and had no sons. So the child imagines that he may be sick in bed and no one is buying him medicine. This poem, by the child not being able to buy sesame cakes, highlights the sadness of the old man who sells hard sesame cakes on the reverse side. It is very moving. There is also a poem describing a seller of hard sesame cakes. The author is Mr. Xu Ji. The general idea is that now no one buys Western pastries, who will still buy hard sesame cakes? These two lines alone highlight the backwardness of Chinese small handicrafts and the sadness of the proletariat. This is another kind of wonderfulness. There is also a poem describing a wet nurse. This poem was published in Free Talk. I do not remember the author clearly. It says that a rural woman sacrifices her own child, but comes to the city to provide milk to the children of the rich. I was very moved at the time. This is also a good poem. Therefore, writing poetry requires a keen eye to see what others have not seen, and also requires rich emotions. The examples mentioned above are all very ordinary things, but after being melted by the poet's mind, they become very beautiful and moving things. Poetry, this thing, does not need to be looked for everywhere. It is right in front of you, but it only depends on whether you have the talent of a poet. There is no need to pore over books or go to various places to look for beautiful scenery. Some people have to look for plum blossoms in the snow in winter, and have to look at the moon in autumn, and then they can have poetry. Those are not poets. Chen Mingqing of the Ming Dynasty said, "There is a kind of ready-made writing between heaven and earth, such as the dimness of clouds and objects, the pouring of rivers and seas, and the various strange trees and birds in front of us. It is up to me to ponder and appreciate them. The Creator is not poor, nor stingy." So it is said that the realm of poetry is very broad. Perhaps some scholars read ten thousand volumes of books and write poetry all day long, but there is not a single good poem. But extremely beautiful lines of poetry can flow from the mouths of rural workers. This is the reason why many people now like to read ballads.

In addition to this, I believe that poetry must also be beautiful. The beauty I am talking about is the beauty of nature, not the beauty of carved words and phrases. For example, the Tang Dynasty poem, "Park the carriage and sit loving the maple forest in the evening, frost leaves are redder than February flowers." The words and phrases are not necessarily that beautiful, but the imagery is very beautiful. This is the beauty of nature. If you carve the words and phrases, you will never have such beautiful poetic meaning. When we read the poems of the ancients, they each have their own style. They are absolutely different. Li Bai's boldness is different from Su Dongpo's boldness. Du Fu is different from Bai Juyi. Tao Yuanming is different from Wang Wei. This is because everyone's nature is different, so poetry can never be learned from others. Even if you learn, you cannot learn it. It is better to see it from yourself. Say what you want to say. Sometimes there may be good poems. Shen Wancun of the Qing Dynasty has a poem that says, "The body is at ease and everything is idle, the sun sets and a village is quiet. Taking the child to the bright moon, watching people's shadows on the wall." It is quite leisurely and pleasing. This is the benefit of being willing to say your own words. The matter is very ordinary. It is just that adults lead children to stroll outside the village at night. However, the imagery is very beautiful. In this way, we can know what poetry is. If someone wants to ask how to write good poetry, how to become a poet? Then I can only ask him to think about it himself. I am sorry that I cannot tell this secret.

Visiting Thousand Buddha Mountain 265

— Liu Ming

If you want me to talk about the benefits of Thousand Buddha Mountain, the benefits are not in itself, because looking at the peaks and shadows from the streets of Jinan, it does not seem to be very beautiful or magnificent. What is so particularly moving about the yellow steep slopes, randomly dotted with ink-black cypress trees? Perhaps in spring and summer, the slopes are covered with green grass, and at dusk, the peaks are smeared with pale blue smoke, making it very beautiful when viewed from a distance. But this is just the scenery common to ordinary mountains, and the characteristics of Thousand Buddha Mountain cannot be recognized from this. But you should slowly climb up the mountain, cross the temple, and climb to the rocky peak. Then turn around and suddenly see the Daming Lake, like a basin, lying in the city of Jinan with its myriad homes and hearths, and the Yellow River, like a belt, winding around the vast wilderness. Only then will you suddenly realize why Thousand Buddha Mountain is loved by tourists and has become a famous scenic spot in northern China. It must be here.

When I went to visit, it was in winter, but because it had not snowed yet, the mountain road was very easy to walk. Moreover, for the past two or three years, I had been living in cities in the south of the Yangtze River, and all the roads I walked were flat. Once I encountered a mountain slope that was not very steep, it was as if I had suddenly met an old friend. Climbing up was really interesting. Although I was a little breathless and tired, when I looked back, the view gradually expanded, and the streets and walls that restricted my body and mind had completely disappeared. I also felt infinite comfort and my spirit was doubled. The mountain road leading to the temple is paved with stone slabs about a foot wide and more than five feet long, and there are short walls built on both sides, which is very clean and tidy. I think this was built specifically for people who worship Buddha. Otherwise, the place behind the temple, where you can only reach the peak and enjoy the scenery to the fullest, would not require tourists with straw sandals and cloth shoes to explore and find their own paths. At the top, the wind is extremely strong. On the one hand, you have to prevent the wind from blowing off your hat, and on the other hand, you have to use your hands to climb on the rocky ground. From time to time, there are also short thorny bushes that catch people's clothes. Therefore, climbing is extremely embarrassing, but the joy and excitement cannot be reduced in the slightest. This is probably because the more dangerous the mountain is to climb, the more it can increase its majesty.

When I reached the top, it was about 3:00 in the afternoon. The trains on the Jiaoji Railway, spraying milky white smoke, came from afar. The way they moved in succession was very similar to a group of black sows walking clumsily in the mud. Compared with the area of the city of Jinan and Daming Lake, it is no longer the "half-city of mountains and half-city of lake" that Lao Can saw. The city has been completely expanded by the infusion of the railway. The countless red roofs in the west are marking the fact that the modernization of the ancient Jinan has reached a considerable degree. In the future, tourists may even be able to sit comfortably on the tram to the foot of the mountain. I only saw some colors and outlines at the top, and thinking about this was after I went down the mountain.

Although I did not see the surging situation of "the Yellow River water coming from the sky" this time, the posture of the snake lazily sleeping in the wilderness was enough for a traveler to rejoice. The river body showed a width of about thirty or forty feet at the turning point, which was light yellow in color compared to the clear water of Daming Lake. The rest was like a light yellow ribbon, and if the river body did not shine slightly, it would be indistinguishable from the northern wilderness.

Going down the mountain is more difficult than going up. You have to be careful not to lose your footing and dare not look into the distance. Only then do you realize the hardship of visiting the mountain, but people are still happy and excited, because the majestic scenery of the north has been painted in their hearts.

Peanut Boat 266

— Shen Shengshi

As soon as winter comes, some out-of-town merchants' boats all dock on the riverbank, a long row of them. There are scale-making boats from Zhejiang, small fishing boats from north of the Yangtze River, umbrella repair boats, and also boats that collect old goods. At the same time, peanut boats also come.

Most of those boats come at a certain time every winter and go back to their hometowns in early spring next year. They plant some rented fields in their hometowns, but because there are too many mouths to feed, they cannot make ends meet. So they come to foreign villages in the winter when there is nothing to do in the fields to do some odd jobs. However, the years are not auspicious, and those small boats cannot do good business in various villages and towns either.

A boat from north of the Yangtze River selling peanuts has been docked on the river beach in front of our school for many days.

Every day after class, I take a leisurely walk along the riverbank with a colleague. There has been a small peanut stall on the riverbank these past few days. On the boat, there are three or four children, five or six years old. Their bodies are tattered and unkempt, as if they had rolled around in a muddy puddle. They have bare feet and their little faces are covered with wrinkles. The riverbank is their playground. They roll stones, bricks, hawthorns, and broken tin cans as toys. They play with those sports equipment energetically.

These ragged children are from that peanut boat.

When the sun sets, an old man in his fifties comes back from the small street carrying a peanut pole. He stops the pole effortlessly on the riverbank and then turns onto the springboard. A middle-aged woman sticks her head out of the reed shed on the boat. Her dirty face shows a trace of hopeful smile, along with a kind voice.

"How many coins did you get?"

The old man's sallow face sinks, he curls his lips, and steps onto the bow of the boat. The boat sways, but he does not answer. He climbs into the boat shed.

He finds a cigarette butt in the reed shed and turns back to the shore. He counts the pile of copper coins thrown in the wooden bucket, frowning as he counts. The three ragged children surround him, calling,

"Old Dad, Old Dad!"

"Old Dad, give me a copper coin!"

He mumbles and scolds all the children away.

We go up to him and chat.

"Old man, how much business do you do every day?"

"Sir, this year is worse than in previous years!"

"Hmm."

"I only exchange for 1,800 cash..."

"These days, rice is more expensive than in previous years! It's hard to live!"

"How many mouths do you have to feed on the boat?"

"Hmm, sir, there are seven people in the family on the boat: the old woman, the eldest son, the daughter-in-law, and three young children. I earn 1,800 cash a day. That's not enough to live on!"

"Is your land north of the Yangtze River also barren?"

"It's barren too! The years are bad, and farming is not lucky. I can't do business either. Last year, I sold peanuts here and earned 4,000 or 5,000 cash a day. That was good. This year, I earn at most 2,000 cash a day!"

He tells us that this small business cannot be done anymore and that he wants to raise some capital to sell sugar cane and oranges.

Smoke rises from the stern of the boat. The old man's young daughter-in-law is warming wild firewood in the stove to cook porridge, blowing fire through a bamboo tube, puffing.

The old man moves the peanut stall on the riverbank back to the boat. It is already getting dark.

On the dim river in the twilight, we watch the old and young of the family of seven on the boat, squatting around the stern, having their supper of a pot of thin porridge.

Requirements for Future Literary Criticism 267

— Hu Sheng

As a characteristic of the Chinese literary world in 1934, I believe that the gradual progress of literary criticism onto the right track should be solemnly put forward.

Serious "author studies" replaced the so-called "impressions," and sharp "book and newspaper criticism" replaced the so-called "after-reading impressions." These are all good phenomena in the past year.

There used to be a group of writers" who believed that the effect of criticism was to make writers "put down their pens," but in fact, good criticism only makes writers more active, and it will lead the latter to move forward on the correct path!

Inheriting the achievements already made in 1934, will literary criticism in 1935 present us with an even more complete posture? We, the readers, sincerely hope so.

In the midst of hope, I would like to put forward a few small requests here:

When building new literary criticism, the introduction of foreign literary theories is really necessary. I remember that Shuimo Bookstore, Guanghua Bookstore, Dajiang Bookstore, etc. used to publish complete sets of literary theory series, but recently, such books seem to have been published too few. Therefore, as in literary creation, large-scale translation and introduction work is also needed in criticism in the future. This is one of my requests.

"Critics should not only criticize others, but also criticize themselves, not only criticize each other, but also self-criticize. All bad criticisms should also be the object of criticism..." Mr. Ren Baige's these few sentences (see Taibai issue 2) are indeed very correct. Today we see...some people hang the big sign of "author study" but only do the work of patching up chapters and sentences, and some others, more clever, cling to Gide, while the more honest ones pull in Babbitt, all shamelessly "criticizing"...Therefore, my second point of request is: On the basis of the new literary criticism, give these colorful theories appropriate blows - criticism!

Literary criticism should certainly make the greatest effort to prevent old writers from becoming corrupt, but at the same time, it should never forget to discover new writers from various newspapers and magazines and guide them forward; and it should not only find promising new writers, but also pay attention to those literary apprentices who are just starting to write, and use various opportunities to help them technically and in terms of subject matter, and encourage them: The constant emergence of new writers is the only way to keep the literary world young. New literary criticism that neglects this aspect will lose its own meaning.

In addition, I have one additional request! I believe that it is not enough to have just a few author studies in general literary magazines and a column of "book review criticism" to undertake the important task of new literary criticism. Therefore, a specialized literary criticism magazine is necessary. Although there were one or two literary criticism magazines in the magazine year of 1934, they were clearly not satisfactory to us. What we hope for is a literary criticism publication that introduces correct foreign theories, constantly reviews our literary world, and can supervise, encourage, and help all writers and beginners!

Flies (6) 268

— By piradnello, translated by Xi Dichén

The sun shone through the horizontal window near the manger, reflecting on a face that no longer looked human: swollen, with the nose missing; the lips were black and distended. The sound of phlegm grew louder, like a howl. In the dark, curly hair, a piece of straw sparkled in the sunlight.

Seeing this scene, the three men seemed to be repelled by terror, stopping abruptly and staring at him. The sound of mule hooves clattered on the cobblestones of the stable. Then, Sa Luo walked up to the dying man and called out intimately:

"Ji La, Ji La, the doctor is here."

Néli struck the mules at the manger; on the nearby wall, there seemed to be a shadow of another animal. It turned out to be: the image of the donkey living in the stable, imprinted on the wall by constant rubbing.

Hearing the second call, Chai Lu stopped the phlegm in his throat. He struggled to open his terrified, already dim, inflamed eyes, and opened his terrible mouth to groan, as if it were burning inside.

"I'm going to die!"

"No, no," Sa Luo replied anxiously, "the doctor is here, we invited him; can you see him?"

"Take me to the village!" Chai Lu said with difficulty and pleadingly, unable to close his lips. "Ah, good God!"

"Okay, look, the mules are here," Sa Luo immediately replied.

"If there's no other way, I'll carry you in my arms, Ji La, I'll take you to the village!" Néli rushed over, bent down and said to him. "Don't be afraid!"

Hearing Néli's gentle voice, Chai Lu turned his head as if he didn't recognize him at first, stared at him with his inflamed eyes, then moved one arm and grabbed Néli's belt.

"Child, is that you?"

"Me? Of course it's me! Are you crying? Don't cry, Ji La, don't cry! It's nothing serious!"

Néli placed one hand on his trembling, sobbing chest, the pitiful sobs unable to break through his throat. Then, Chai Lu choked, shook his head violently, raised one hand, grabbed Néli's neck, and pulled him towards himself.
