Shanghai News Local Supplement

Discussions

The Liberation from Depression 269

— Bǐng

Young people in today's world, whether employed or unemployed, share a very common problem: depression. This is indeed a sign of the times; global turmoil, social darkness, and the decline of human relationships are all wounding the hearts of young people in a chain reaction. Under these circumstances, it is practically impossible not to fall into depression.

Young people are passionate and full of fiery blood, just like Tao Jianping in "Peach and Plum Calamity." They dare to speak and act, willing to sacrifice themselves for justice, regardless of other consequences. However, reality is precisely the opposite, so the depression of young people mostly begins here.

This responsibility should be assigned to society. However, there is also a large proportion of young people whose depression does not stem from this source. After spending some time in society, they feel indifferent to everything, yet the shadow of depression still covers each of their hearts, deeply. This requires seeking solutions from within oneself.

When young people fall into depression, the danger is not only that depression leads to pessimism, and pessimism leads to negativity, self-abandonment, and then to depravity and suicide. This is an inevitable trend. When a young person reaches this point, the danger is obvious. This is not only a sacrifice for the young person themselves but also a major loss for society.

This requires remediation. From a broad perspective, it is certainly a social issue, but there is also a need for rigorous self-examination and efforts to recover. This is a question of personal responsibility. Many people are trapped in a state of depression, but they can ultimately use reasonable methods to safely navigate through it and reach the shore of success. What is the method of liberating oneself from depression? In my opinion, the only way is for our spirit to have something to which to attach itself.

Christians are all cheerful, and monks are also broad-minded and physically robust. This is the effect of entrusting one's spirit to religious belief. Hermits and men of letters devote themselves to landscapes, fishing, drinking wine, and composing poetry, and then their depression is alleviated. Throughout history, countless writers and scientists, all those whose spirits have been entrusted to something, have lived their lives happily and achieved extraordinary accomplishments. Otherwise, they spend their days frowning and living a miserable life, never tasting a bit of the sweetness of life. Regarding the entrustment of the spirit, Yuan Zhonglang explained it most thoroughly in a letter to his friend Li Ziran. I have excerpted a few words here to serve as a conclusion:

"…Human emotions must be entrusted to something to be joyful. Therefore, some entrust themselves to chess, some to beauty, some to skills, and some to literature. The enlightened people of ancient times were a level higher simply because their emotions had a place to be entrusted, and they were unwilling to waste time in a superficial and empty manner. Every time I see people without a place to entrust their emotions, they are busy all day long, as if they have lost something, worrying about nothing, and not enjoying the scenery. Even they themselves do not know why. This is a living hell. What else can be said about iron beds, copper pillars, mountains of knives, and trees of swords? Pity, pity!…"

Fantasy 270

— Jiǎ Chén

People are all bound by the colorful realities of life, and this bondage is inescapable for anyone. At the same time, reality is unsatisfactory for eight or nine out of ten people, seen as a net of suffering. Therefore, the only way to temporarily relieve the fatigue of reality and leisurely enter a state of joy beyond reality is through fantasy, or, it can also be said, ideals. Therefore, everyone likes to be close to fantasy, fantasizing about the brilliance of the days ahead, fantasizing that there will be splendid fruits of dreams in the future. Thus, an invisible, magnificent utopia stands in their minds. They use the sweetness of fantasy to smooth out the wounds of reality, painting as many colorful images as possible on the fantasy to forget the various sorrows of reality. Therefore, the existence of fantasy is worth cherishing. Almost no one does not regard fantasy as a more intimate companion than anything else and is unwilling to leave it for a moment. If you can be closer to it for one more minute, you can gain one more minute of comfort and tenderness. During this gained time, you are also isolating yourself from the suffering of reality. Conversely, if you cannot be close to fantasy, you will lose some enjoyment of comfort and tenderness, while on the other hand, you will endure some more pain and torment from reality.

Like being so busy during the day that you are dizzy and dazed, barely having time to stop. The entanglement of the day really makes your soul numb. What joy is there to talk about? Moreover, in the bustling human affairs of the day, you often encounter various frustrating and unpleasant events for no reason. When evening comes, you stretch lazily and fall onto the bed, exhaling a long, stuffy breath. At this moment, fantasy, like a woman in a beautiful dress filled with fragrance, smiles and lightly steps into your heart, making a sweet visit. Then, you unconsciously close your eyes slightly, as if awake but also as if confused. In that instant, the thick dust and fatigue of life that have been pressing on your soul during the day have completely fallen away. At the same time, you are thus intoxicated in the gentle cradle of fantasy.

When you encounter some disappointments in the real environment, or spiritual unhappiness, and there is no way to restore it with human effort, the only method is to seek it from the gift of fantasy. Whatever you cannot find in real life, no matter how rare, even a desire that is forever a dream, you can get everything from fantasy. Fantasy is indeed an indispensable place of rest for the human soul, changing your gray feeling towards a joyless real life, further strengthening your interest, deepening your attachment to life, and encouraging you to move forward.

However, fantasy should not be too boundless and limitless. The most appropriate thing is to slowly stretch along the edge of reality. If it deviates from reality too far, as vague as the clouds in the sky above the sea, then permanent fantasy is just fantasy, not easily turning into the rich fruit of reality. Then, always fantasizing throughout your life will inevitably lead to feeling empty throughout your life. In this way, all fantasies become bubbles, coming without a trace and going without a trace, ultimately leaving only a faint, seemingly confused wisp of blue smoke in your heart.

Therefore, although fantasy is a relaxing cradle for the human soul, it must also have weight. Being too empty and vague will not only lose the warmth and comfort of fantasy, but may also cause infinite frustration. If you have already suffered the disasters of reality, and still feel sadness because of fantasy, it will be even more unbearable. Therefore, it is okay to indulge in fantasy, but do not completely deviate from your actual life and abilities. Like climbing a mountain, first estimate your strength, then step by step go up. Stop when you can't climb, don't force yourself to climb again. Because if you fall, it's not a joke. Fantasy is also like this. Fantasizing about the Three Divine Mountains, so unattainable, is ultimately still distressing.

After Seeing the Public Performance of Peiming Girls' High School 271

— Luó Píng

Although it is the dead of winter, the public performances of various schools are very lively. The successive public performances of the John, Guanghua, Zhirenyong, Liangjiang, and Guohua drama clubs may not have achieved much, but at least they are a sign of vitality in the theatrical world.

This time, the public performance of Peiming Girls' High School did not have enough time for preparation beforehand, relying on the efforts of a few people, but the results obtained were quite satisfactory.

In order to raise funds for the construction of a school building, the performance was held over two days. The reporter only saw the program on the last day.

In addition to the songs and dances influenced by Li Jinhui and the magic tricks performed by elementary school students, three relatively meaningful plays were performed. In the afternoon: (1) Before Lunch (2) Oppression (3) By the Huangpu River; In the evening, only the latter two were performed. The successful ones were only the latter two plays.

Because they are all old plays, it seems unnecessary to talk about the scripts themselves here.

Compared from the stage, "Oppression" was better than "By the Huangpu River". In "Oppression," due to the interest of the story and the excellence of the actors, it was able to capture the emotions of the audience.

Shen Ruchen, who played the female tenant, and Li Bihua, who played the male tenant, performed very hard. Their rich dramatic talent and fluent, clear dialogue were the biggest reasons for the success of this play. In particular, it is worth surprising that Shen Ruchen achieved such great success without having undergone many rehearsals. Li Bihua often sticks his tongue out when speaking, which is a minor flaw. Tang Renliang, who played the old lady, and Hu Lanzhi, who played the old nanny, were both able to match the identities of the characters in the play. Zhang Cai's portrayal of the police officer, often putting his hands in his pockets, was also a shortcoming. The performance in the evening was more complete than the performance in the afternoon.

The next is "By the Huangpu River". In my opinion, this opera is not very suitable for female students to perform. Although this is almost subjective, on the one hand, because there is a kind of rugged style of dockworkers in this play, although it is not absolutely impossible to express it, at least it will lose a little color.

The second reason is that the painful groans, the cries of life, the resentful songs, and the heroic shouts of the dockworkers here should be sung by a bass, but this has become a problem. Because of this, the performance of the entire play was affected. The actors were all average, but not serious enough. Zheng Senlan, who played the old man, was better.

As for "Before Lunch," due to the lengthy dialogue and the sparse rehearsals, the effect of the performance of this play was inferior to "Oppression" and "By the Huangpu River." The actors did not pay much attention to small actions. The more commendable one was Shen Aizhen, who played the third sister.

All the shortcomings cannot cover up the achievements of this public performance. At least we discovered many girls with dramatic talent, adding a hope for the future of this theatrical world.

Square and Round 272

— Xiǎo Yīng

Winter comes, autumn goes; winter goes, spring comes, just like that, circling eternally.

It’s really fast, in a blink of an eye, another year has passed in a muddle, just like a dream. What was the situation in the dream? At that time, it was clear, but after that? I can't answer, leaving myself with a thin gauze-like net!

No matter how thin the net is, what cannot be denied is that the wrinkles on my forehead are increasing and deepening... Looking at myself in the mirror, I thought, "Ah, you heartstrings of a wanderer, what do you hope for? Your complexion is taking your gray fate to the edge of the tomb…" Involuntarily, a wave of sourness welled up in my heart, reaching my throat and then choking me.

Isn’t that right? The New Year's streets are bustling with activity. That group of people moving are countless heads!

Page 21

Is that a happy appearance? But who can be sure that there are no bitter tears inside!

Originally, when it came to this time, I had to find a way to hide, otherwise, the different faces of the creditors would really be too much to bear. But this year, I didn't hide. I feel that those different faces are lovely. Why hide from that typical expression?

×××

Some people say that the South is a paradise, because the climate, scenery, and so on in the South give people a pleasant atmosphere and feeling.

That's right, I think. Isn’t that right? Although it is in the cold winter, the vegetable gardens in Jiangnan are still lush and green. Although the weeping willows by the creek have withered, the river is still flowing nearby!

Here, I miss the North, which I have been away from for seven years.

In fact, the North and the South are obviously different. In the North, it is now the time to freeze. No, the heavy snow flying about is probably over the ankles.

Although the North is bleak, it has a unique charm. After the heavy snow, in the season of fierce wind, isn't there a large group of men and women skating at the ice rink in front of Yilan Hall? Laughing in all sorts of ways? But, this is the charm of the North! How fast, in a blink of an eye, another seven years have passed since I left!

Longing is deeply buried.

Talking About Killing 273

— Gē Bái

The New Year is coming, and every family is killing chickens and ducks. Suddenly, a whim came over me, and I thought of Mr. Feng Zikai's "Protecting Life Collection". My aunt, who fasted and chanted scriptures all year round, asked me to buy it and send it back from the post office. My uncle died young in middle age, and a posthumous child died before the age of two. My aunt complained about her bad fate and vowed to fast and chant scriptures all year round to redeem herself. Moreover, every year she went to Putuo Mountain in Hangzhou to pay homage and offer incense. She never shook her head at the donation book of the monks. She released fish and snakes, and chanted some kind of scripture, saying that they would never be caught again. With such painstaking efforts, she still fell from the Buddha hall last year and followed her deceased husband to the underworld. On the way to the hospital, the string of prayer beads was still tightly held. It is said that after she died, it could not be removed. Thinking of that "Protecting Life Collection," I couldn't help but chant "Amen" non-stop.

This year, I attended two banquets: (1) a wedding, (1) a full-month celebration, both of which were vegetarian banquets. The host of the former was a great philanthropist. He said that he was unwilling to slaughter many living beings for his son's wedding, partly to create blessings for his descendants and partly to create blessings for the guests' descendants. This statement won many flattering words praising public virtue and many stories of good rewards for those who refrain from killing and release living beings. Thus, the host and guests dispersed happily. The latter was for an elderly couple who had a son, and it was obtained from the Goddess of Mercy who sends children in some famous mountain. He also said that he was unwilling to slaughter many living beings for his thirty-day-old child, so I listened to many stories of black fish repaying kindness again.

At that time, I was indeed moved. Thinking of the cruel images of killing chickens and ducks, philanthropists naturally could not bear to eat their meat after hearing their cries!

However, I was not born into a good family, and I don't know how to use any means to make money. To support myself, I also have to be slaughtered by others. Can this little bit of aroused emotion put on a mask to talk about refraining from killing and releasing living beings?

Moreover, reading the newspaper, I saw news of "exchanging children for food". Although I did not witness it with my own eyes, as long as I imagine it like killing chickens and ducks, the cries of many children who can shout "Mom, Dad" are a step further than the cries of "Ooo, gaa, gaa". I don't know what philanthropists who advocate refraining from killing and releasing living beings and creating blessings for their descendants think?

A sudden whim is ultimately just a sudden whim. In order to celebrate that my mental effort has not been completely squeezed out this year, the kitchen is already preparing to slaughter a chicken to eat a relatively sumptuous dinner. I no longer have the leisure to glance at the big rooster tied with straw on its feet struggling on the ground!

Heart Net 274

— Yě Fēi

I have been suffering from insomnia these past few nights. I don't know why? I don't understand myself. I toss and turn in bed, really suffering to the extreme. In the morning, I can't get up because I'm dizzy and have a headache. But for the sake of life, I have no choice but to get up and struggle. However, I can't cheer up. I have no appetite and can't hear anything. I'm dizzy all day long.

I took a mirror to look at myself and felt that the flesh on my face had been shaved off a lot in the past few days. The two lifeless eyes were also deeply sunken in their sockets. My complexion was terribly pale! I couldn't help but throw the mirror in my hand on the ground and sighed, throwing my dead-looking limbs on the bed.

My wife was very worried about me, but she didn't dare to ask me too much, for fear that I would lose my temper. She asked me several times if I wanted to see a doctor, but I always shook my head and mumbled, without saying a word. She was very bored and didn't understand what illness I had. The day before yesterday, she finally secretly asked a doctor to come and see me, and I didn't say yes or no. He took my pulse and said that I was restless. As long as I rested and recuperated peacefully and suffered less stimulation, I would slowly get better. But! It is really difficult for me to cut off my thoughts. These past few days, not only have I been unable to rest and recuperate peacefully, but I have also been thinking wildly more and more. So my illness has not only not been alleviated, but it is even progressing into a deeper realm! Yesterday, Dr. Zhou also came and gave me a prescription. I saw a very melancholy look on his face. Later, he only spoke a few words lightly to my wife:

"He needs to rest and recuperate peacefully. If he continues like this, it will be very dangerous..." But I heard it very clearly. I am not afraid of death. What I hate most is living half-dead. I don't want to rest and recuperate peacefully. Although I want to live, I can't stop the coming of death. However, when my heart can still think and still beat, I still want to think and beat. Naturally, when it can't think and stops beating, then everything will be over!

What's the point of being a human? A life worse than a cow or a horse, a mechanical life! The world is so unfair and snobbish. Human beings are so cold and cruel. All the encounters are vicious, fanged, blood-sucking ghosts. My blood has been sucked dry by them. I feel that my surroundings are full of nets of fear!

I deeply feel that the past was a dream, a nightmare! The present is still a dream, and the future may still be a dream!

The dreams of life are interwoven into a net, a dense heart net, to hold my heart. It is stretched very tight. It won't jump or open and close. Insomnia is still getting worse day by day. At night, the heart net shrinks even more severely. Therefore, I can't sleep after all. But in order to delay the moment before death, I still have to live, so I have to reluctantly get up and struggle!

Hometown Sound 275

— Jizi

One chilly, gloomy dusk. I, alone, carrying a heart attacked by the depression of life, went to the residence of a hometown friend I hadn't seen in seven years.

Entering the door, in a small, clean upstairs room, under the pale light, I and this long-separated friend, held hands tightly, looked at each other, speechless. After a while, he put a hand on my shoulder, and the other smoothed the long hair hanging on both sides of his cheeks. Affectionately and surprisedly, he said:

"Oh my, you've grown so big! I almost didn't recognize you... Your face is too haggard, too... well, how are you living?"

We sat down on the edge of the bed, which was close to the wall and the desk. Drinking Emei tea, eating melon seeds, we talked freely about everything since our separation, both happily and sadly. Later, we talked about the hometown in recent years, from the advance levy to the grain tax of the 80th year of the Republic, to how the people opposed paying the newly levied "emotional donation" this year, from planting opium to the rise and fall of the three forces of "blackening," "corruption," and "reddening," the decline of big landlords to becoming waiters in opium dens, farmers starving and becoming beggars, and those running morphine factories becoming rich...

"Some people say, 'The thick coal smoke smell in Chongqing city used to be, but now it is overwhelmed by the fragrance of opium.'" Is our city the same way? I asked, lying on the bed, intentionally or unintentionally.

"Of course, it's no different. Oh, this summer, for a few days, my nostrils stopped being stuffed with this smoky atmosphere," he said, recalling.

I was very surprised and sat up to take a sip of tea.

"What? Is some military commander again arresting opium addicts to hang them?"

He pursed his lips and smiled bitterly.

"What military commander! Don't you know Sichuan is a demonic place!"

I eagerly asked him to tell me what was going on, and he frowned and sighed, saying:

"It's like this: It is said that on the nineteenth day of the sixth lunar month, a strange old beggar woman came to our county. She didn't want the money people gave her, nor did she want rice, she didn't want anything, just shouted along the street, advising people to quit opium immediately. Later, she knelt in front of an opium shop, repeatedly urging people not to smoke, and saying that those who didn't listen and didn't quit opium would all not live past the middle of the seventh month... Later, the opium shop owner, fearing that he would scare away his customers, came out to drive the old beggar woman away, but she stubbornly insisted on not leaving, and finally the owner kicked her, and she immediately disappeared. Later…"

Speaking of this, he suddenly stopped. He seemed unwilling to say more about these ghostly and absurd things, staring at the melon seed shells in front of him without speaking. I anxiously pressed him:

"What happened later? Finish the story!"

He glanced at me and said in a low voice:

"The next afternoon, the opium shop owner who kicked the beggar woman suddenly died of heatstroke. So, some people made a fuss and spread rumors that the old beggar woman from yesterday was an incarnation of Guanyin Bodhisattva, and the owner was punished for insulting the Bodhisattva... Suddenly, the whole city was in an uproar, and all the 'retail shops' – opium shops – all closed their doors, and all the opium users hid their smoking paraphernalia, and some even burned them! Later, the county government panicked because they couldn't collect opium tax. Then, the government issued a notice: 'No one is allowed to spread rumors to confuse the public... or endanger public order.' In less than ten days, those opium addicts started smoking again!"

I burst out laughing, and he laughed too.

In the cold wind, with excitement and reluctance to part, I said goodbye to my friend and started on my way home. Right now, the curtain of memory still reflects...

"…Sichuan is a demonic place…"

These words. I don't understand why people are fascinated by demons and still haven't woken up!

Pingtan (Stringed Musical Narrative) 278

Yao Xiao'an Wang Pingqiu - Pearl Pagoda

Zhongxi (1040) 10:00 AM to 11:00 AM

Opening: "New Year"

Gentle spring breeze is everywhere. Every household is setting off firecrackers and gongs. The fourth and fifth days of the New Year are consecutive. The five roads of the God of Wealth are greeted a lot. Fortune, prosperity, and longevity are all present. Chicken, fish, and meat fill the plate. Pine needles, cypress twigs, and wintergreen leaves. Bidding farewell to the old year and welcoming the new year are indispensable. Thousands of households respect them. The road gods do not have much effort. Going to people's homes doesn't necessarily mean going in person. Profitable market attracts wealth instead. There are candles and incense often. There is no tea or wine. Zhenyi Xuantan is afraid to come. The golden wheel is not greedy. My family wants to receive the God of Wealth. I don't care about the Dragon Boat Festival on the fifth day. That is to say, Zhong Kui is marrying his sister. The road god asks for a mother-in-law. Therefore, we know that Zhong Jinshi is. The closest relatives are the brother-in-law. The brother-in-law by marriage. Naturally, there are things to help with. Be sure to wish the brother-in-law a happy birthday. Arrange public shares to play Sheng and sing songs. The wealth system envoy also has a share. Everyone will never look down on me. Make a fortune like a shuttle.

Li Yanqiu - Legend of the White Snake

Yuanchang (1120) 11:30 AM to 12:15 PM

The scenery of West Lake is beautiful and magnificent. Outstanding people and earth produce beautiful women. The girl has the appearance of a celestial being. Her studies have been completed to a high level. Her mind is exquisite and clever. She likes the word "vanity" the most. Her family doesn't worry about food, clothing, and shelter. Her parents are old and like to meditate. Treat her like a bright pearl in their hands and spoil her so much. At home, she studies on her own and accompanies her parents. Since childhood, she was betrothed to a fellow villager. He is a talented painter. The young man is gentle and unpretentious. His family is poor and extremely wronged. They are in love with each other. They often wander at West Lake. The red sun sets in the west, they return hand in hand. Their deep affection is sincere. Hoping that they can become a couple soon. The talented and beautiful couple get together. People praise them. They all say that the girl is beautiful. A good thing is always frustrated. Suddenly, the situation changes for no reason. The girl meets a handsome young man. He has a doctorate and his surname is Han. Moreover, his father holds a high position in the political world. He is famous for his talents. He dislikes the painter. The old promise has been completely forgotten. They are sweet and intimate. They often boat together on West Lake. At this time, their love is fiery. They are engaged. The former lover is like a stranger. He did not expect that the doctor's heart is unpredictable. He abandoned the old love and went to pursue a new love. He abandoned the girl without any news. They scattered the mandarin ducks. Women should never be greedy for vanity.

National Studies 279

Wang Bingmei, Female Scholar, Tang Poetry

Huaxing (1260) 9:00 AM to 10:00 AM

Listening to Dong Fu Playing the Barbarian Reed Pipe, Zhu Ji Speaks to the Palace Attendant, Li Zhen

Cai Wenji created the sound of the barbarian reed pipe in the past,

One strum had eighteen beats.

Barbarians shed tears wetting the edge of the grass;

The Han envoy was heartbroken facing the returning travelers.

The ancient garrison station was vast, the beacon fire was cold;

The great wilderness was gloomy, and the flying rain was white.

First sweep away the shang string, then the jiao yu,

Emulating the sound of autumn leaves shaking with fright.

Master Dong, is in touch with the divine,

Deep in the pine forest, the goblin listens secretly.

Slow or fast, he responds to all;

Flicking back and forth, it seems as if he has feelings.

In the empty mountain, a hundred birds scatter and gather;

Ten thousand miles of floating clouds are sometimes shady and sometimes sunny.

The mournful cry of a lost gosling in the night;

The desperate sound of a barbarian child missing its mother!

The river seems to cleanse its waves;

The birds also cease their cries.

Birds are tribal homeland,

Sorrowful cries of Suosun Chan are born.

The secluded sound changes, and the lyrics suddenly become free and unrestrained,

The long tide blows through the forest, and the rain falls on the tiles.

Bursting springs rustle as they fly to the treetops;

Young deer run quietly under the hall.

Chang'an City is connected to the East Annex,

Phoenix Pond faces the Green Locked Door.

A man of great talent breaks away from fame and wealth,

Day and night, I look forward to him arriving with his zither.

Shenbao Local Supplement - Movie Special

A Brief History of the Development of Cinema (1) 281

— Wen Ying

(1) The Audience is the Master of the Film Industry

Audiences, the film industry is your industry. The reason why the film industry has reached its current level of development is that you have created it. The joys and sorrows of the audience are the laws that entrepreneurs abide by. From the very beginning of cinema, when a few "idle people" pooled some money, purchased a clumsy film projector, and shook out the dancing shadows of people in a dilapidated empty house, to the indescribable prosperity of today, the audience has always been the dictator and ruler of the film industry.

In the year 1900, whoever mentioned motion pictures would laugh. They considered themselves knowledgeable people and disdained to consider such trivial matters. Bankers turned a deaf ear when they heard that someone wanted to borrow capital from them to start a film business. Some poor people pooled their life savings and invested in the film industry, and their friends called them crazy. But when the day came, everyone ran to a dilapidated house to watch motion pictures. They saw that the film really did move, and everyone was surprised. They saw with their own eyes a train coming towards them. They saw with their own eyes a girl with hair curls who made them cry for her one moment and laugh through their tears the next. That was the later world-famous Mary Pickford. The people of that generation found those crude, jerky films very interesting. They unknowingly nurtured the beginning of a large enterprise, because the big bankers on the street knew that they liked to watch that kind of thing, so they loosened the strings of their money bags and began to invest in the film industry. Therefore, from the very beginning, the film industry belonged to the film audience.

Around 1923, the American film industry had already developed greatly. Samuel Goldwyn once gathered the most famous film critics from the American press and magazines, gave them generous salaries, and asked them to judge the merits of films before they were publicly released. As a result, the experiment was a complete failure, because what they thought was good, the audience didn't like to watch, and what they thought was bad, the audience welcomed. From this, we can see that the will of the audience cannot be directed by any expert. If an entrepreneur spends countless amounts of money to bring out a star, and the audience likes it and tells their friends, and everyone says it's good, then the entrepreneur's money is not wasted. Otherwise, if the audience just frowns slightly, the star will immediately lose their footing, and the entrepreneur's money will be like throwing it into the water. The income at the ticket office is Hollywood's only standard for estimating the value of stars, and that standard is determined by when everyone in the audience opens their wallets to buy tickets.

Therefore, all of you in the audience are the masters of the film industry, and the film industry is not an ordinary industry, but one of the six major enterprises in the United States. But in other industries, your position is not as important, whether it is in the steel industry, the cotton yarn industry, or the silk industry. Because the film industry is your own industry, it will be very beneficial and perhaps very interesting for you to know how the film industry started, how it developed, who are the heroes in the history of cinema, and a brief overview of the past thirty years, because the history of cinema is full of glory and romance. It contains lively and active characters, successful and failed experiences, sad and disappointing grievances, and ecstatic pleasures. We are in a modern position and can look back and unite the past traces, but our pioneers did not have the foresight to look forward. This is where our modern situation is superior. (To be continued)

Film Review

Review of "Oliver Twist" 282

— Ling He

Oliver Twist｜Cathay｜

After "Les Misérables," here is another novel by Dickens brought to the screen.

Regarding Dickens, I once mentioned him in my writing about "Les Misérables," and there is no need to introduce him now. Although he is not a very great writer, Chinese readers are very familiar with him. As for this "Oliver Twist," there was once a translation by Lin Qinnan, entitled "The Thief's History." Moreover, in the silent film era, "Oliver Twist" gave people a very deep impression.

We have repeatedly pointed out that the adaptation of literary works to the screen, in addition to illustrating the lack of themes in American films, is mainly because certain literary works can still coincide with the subjective requirements of filmmakers in the 1920s and 1930s. For example, due to the rapid collapse of the economic foundation at the current stage, there are tens of thousands of children wandering the streets and homeless in every city. Of course, they have to live. They have no other way of life other than begging or stealing. This phenomenon is naturally a hidden worry in the eyes of social figures, but they have no way to seek a thorough solution. Therefore, reformism is their only means. Therefore, the works of the British reformist Dickens have been repeatedly adapted.

Now, let us further explore Dickens' style from "Oliver Twist" itself, although this is through the screenwriting of Ending Mechan, and it is not easy to fully glimpse the face of the novel.

Like all reformers, Dickens saw the cruelty or lack of compassion of the noble class of the time. This is evident in the fact that the child Oliver could not get a penny when he asked the gentleman in the carriage for money, and that he received brutal punishment when he wanted another bowl of soup in the orphanage. Furthermore, the satirical depiction of the high-ranking group when Oliver was questioned in the orphanage is full of the author's resentment.

Similarly, Dickens also strongly disliked the group of thieves, such as Oliver's being beaten and the brutality of the thief leader Bill Sikes. Although he was pathologically depicting them, he gave some degree of sympathy to their being forced by life. Then, under this observation, Dickens put forward his own subjective views. That is, he disguised Oliver's grandfather and appeared among the rich, and he especially emphasized the kindness and benevolence of Bill Sikes' wife among the thieves. Finally, the wandering child was saved. The above-mentioned theme is really too suitable for American filmmakers.

However, in the expression of the film, it is not enough in any aspect. The director did the first few scenes very well, and the climax later was okay, but it was not expressed in many places. If it is said that the protagonist child is very pitiful, then this must be added to the audience's imagination to understand. The director cannot give the audience direct stimulation. Of course, it can also be seen that the child's acting skills are not very good, and the other actors in the play, such as the two larger little thieves, are unnatural performances. However, the personality of the old man in prison and the big thief are written quite vividly. As for the dullness and obscurity, it is naturally an inevitable result.

A Critique of "The Trail Drive" 283

— You Jing

"The Trail Drive" | Carlton

Using the simple and stalwart life of herdsmen in the vast American West as its material, weaving in elements of chivalry and adding some romantic interludes, the script produced has been common since the silent film era. Even now, with the development of sound films, in addition to performances featuring seductive jazz songs and dances, extravagant and decadent urban landscapes, and luxurious and decadent lifestyles, there are also many productions that draw on the aforementioned quiet and simple rural backgrounds and the bold and forthright stories of herdsmen. It's just a pity that few of them are good.

In fact, in recent years, when four-fifths of the earth has been plunged into turmoil, and during a period when the economic panic, livestock, slaughterhouse, and leather industries have all suffered great calamities, those herdsmen living between primitive modes of production and the emerging depression, the grim realities they face and the past events they recall, are full of stories of heroism and tragedy, startling and shocking real stories that could be made into excellent films. However, limited by the views and techniques of the producers, they either unrealistically seek plots from fantasies or emphasize the entanglements of men and women or the heroic deeds of individuals, resulting in the production of vulgar works that are either cliché or inaccurate.

This "Chivalrous Couple" is no exception. It writes about economic downturn, when farmers' livestock are unwanted. John (a livestock dealer), although willing to buy, is refused credit by the bank.

It would have been more commendable if the plot had unfolded with John proposing to the herdsmen to issue bonds first, and then pay cash after the livestock were sold in New Mexico, the herdsmen having no choice but to agree to these terms, and with John colluding with the governor to issue sales permits in advance, swallowing the money, and refusing to recognize the bonds.

But how did Alan Jain, the writer and director of "Chivalrous Couple," understand and handle the problems he captured from reality? He did not move towards the "peak" of the script from the life struggles of the vast group of herdsmen under this phenomenon, completing his masterpiece. He singled out "Gampton, who is naturally loyal and chivalrous, works on John's ranch, taking care of livestock and escorting them for sale," to desperately force John to pay the herdsmen the money they deserved for their livestock, for the herdsmen, and for his lover, Virginia.

Firstly, in terms of Gampton being naturally loyal, how could he turn against his master? The screen does not show a sufficient and appropriate process. Instead, it only shows "miraculous" strength, fighting against dozens of thugs, being invulnerable in a hail of bullets, exaggerating to the point of mythology with "leaping over the Tan Stream on horseback," crossing cliffs, wading through rivers, and hitting the mark every time with his returning gun. The coincidental and unrealistic performances, such as the enemies tying him to the door, letting him break down the door panel and fall out of the window onto two horses that carry him away, and John's repentance, have already elevated the entire play into the realm of fantasy. How could it bear another "riverbank romance" love tail, falling into the cliché of a mediocre and old-fashioned Happy Ending!

In terms of performance, generally speaking, it has not escaped the old-fashioned martial arts romance film. Some of the scenes depicting the lives of herdsmen have some merit, such as the natural scenery of tents in the wilderness, cattle herds, covered wagons, rivers, clouds and moon, wind and dust, and the primitive lifestyle are written in an extremely simple, soft, concise, and beautiful way. Several scenes of folk songs and dances are also adopted and handled quite adorably.

Apart from Ken Maynard, who plays Gampton, taking the stage with the banner of a martial arts star, showing off his fighting skills and horsemanship, William Gould, who plays the villainous merchant John, is relatively better. The expressions of the herdsmen's worries, anger, and joy, and the performance of the mob, show the director's efforts.

Hopes for the New Year! 284

— Lin Qin

I hope that all Chinese film magazines will stop their literary brawls and do their best to introduce domestic films, becoming faithful reporters.

I hope that entrepreneurs will discard their "business eyes" and produce some educational works for the sake of the nation and society.

I hope that directors will not be too arrogant, looking down on ordinary employees, while at the same time not putting effort into art themselves.

I hope that employees will conduct themselves with integrity and make the film industry bright and brilliant.

I hope that actresses will not do broadcasting, fashion shows, or become dancers, or...

I hope that Chinese people will watch more Chinese films and fewer foreign films.

Film Novel

The Policeman Rides the Dragon (White Lies) (3) 286

— Xin Zhi

After the local news editor left, Mitchell was about to look at a few other manuscripts when his secretary walked in, looking flustered, with a pale face, as if he had seen a ghost. He told Mitchell, "There's a man outside who wants to see you. His name is Dan Oliver. He won't say what he wants to see you about, but I... I... I think he looks quite fierce." Mitchell leaned back in his chair, his face suspicious and indecisive. After a moment, he resolutely said, "Tell him to come in!"

Dan Oliver came in. He was a small, thin man with gray hair, a face full of worry, revealing the fierce fire burning inside him, causing his eyes to sink and his cheekbones to protrude. Mitchell stared at him with wide eyes, feeling uneasy in his heart. He looked at Dan Oliver's hand inserted in his pocket. He thought if he would be so afraid. But he wasn't. His hand remained motionless opposite him. Mitchell then opened him up and said, "Do you want to see me?" The man said, "Are you the chief editor, Mr. Mitchell?" Mitchell said, "That's right, I am." The man said, "I am Dan Oliver. Your newspaper is going to publish a piece of news about me. I beg you not to publish it. Please give me a chance to repay the money I embezzled." His dry voice showed the anxiety in his heart. Mitchell slowly shook his head and said, "I'm sorry. It's too late now. You stole so much money, my readers should know about it." As Mitchell spoke, tears streamed from Dan Oliver's eyes. He shouted, "Just to satisfy the low desires of the general readership, you are going to tear a person's life to pieces like this?" Mitchell coldly said, "Why didn't you think about your life before you stole that money? I'm just providing my readers with true news." Oliver roared, "True news! True news! Do you know what true news is! You provide the general public with shallow knowledge with news of rape, adultery, and plunder, exaggerating and praising it every day. Now I have also become your sacrificial victim, just for you to have a large-font headline, to stir people's ears and eyes, you have cut off the path of my life." Mitchell sat in the big chair, pretending to be calm, and said, "Oliver, there's no need for us to discuss this issue any further."

Oliver's attitude suddenly became ferocious. He took a step forward, pointed the gun in his pocket at Mitchell, and said hatefully, "Okay! I'll give you another big headline—the biggest headline of the year. I'm standing here, waiting for your newspaper to be published. If my affair is published inside, I won't be human if I don't put a few holes in you!" Mitchell still leaned back in his chair without changing his expression. He looked very calmly at the person in front of him, but his brain was working rapidly. The person in front of him was a thug. He had come with determination, that was beyond doubt. But since he did not take drastic action, he still had time to adjust to him and fool him a little. At this time, Oliver was standing at the door, with his back to the open door. Mitchell waited quietly for the opportunity to reason with him again. But as soon as he glanced out of the door, his heart sank.

It turned out that his daughter Joan, wearing a new dress, walked in gracefully. As soon as she came in, she shouted, "Hello, Dad, give me some money." That was her usual state, like a spoiled young lady. She suddenly saw a stranger standing behind her. She was startled, and then said, "Oh, I'm sorry, I'll come back later." Oliver took out his gun and pointed it at her! "That's right. You wait. Wait here." Joan glanced at him, then walked gracefully behind her father and stood there. At this time, Mitchell's face turned even paler. Joan, his daughter, was also in a very dangerous situation with him. If this madman opened fire, wouldn't father and daughter die together? Suddenly, the phone on his desk rang. Mitchell looked at Oliver's face, as if asking him if he could answer it or not. (To be continued)

(5) Recent Situation of Lianyungang 288

— (Ming, Photographer)

The construction project of Lianyungang is nearing completion. The foundation of the wharf is extremely solid. Since the start of berthing of ships on October 1st of last year, cargo transportation has been thriving day by day. The average monthly volume of cargo in and out exceeds 10,000 tons, all of which are local products from Jiangsu, Shandong, Shaanxi, and Henan provinces. Currently, only one 3,000-ton seagoing vessel can be berthed. The remaining engineering works are still in progress. The entire dredging project is scheduled to be completed in the spring of this year, reliably providing berthing for eight ships. The Longhai Railway and China Merchants Bureau are handling water-land intermodal transport to complete the shipping development plan. It is planned to sail three routes: one from Lianyungang directly to Yunggand one from Shanghai directly to Guangzhou.

(8) Exhibition of Coins from Past Dynasties 289

— (Xu Tianzhang, Photographer)

Yang Wenqi, a recluse who collects coins from past dynasties, held an exhibition of Chinese coins from various dynasties at the Shanghai YMCA in Baxianqiao from the 29th to the 31st of last month. More than 5,000 types of ancient and modern coins were displayed. In terms of form, they were divided into knives, cloth, and springs. In terms of writing, there were ancient seal script, big seal script, small seal script, official script, running script, and cursive script. In terms of raw materials, there were five-alloy mixed metal, red copper, purple copper, brass, white copper, copper-iron, lead, gold, and silver. Mr. Yang compiled and collated them according to the order of the dynasties, adding detailed notes. It can be viewed as a history of coins and can also provide a glimpse into the progress of China's culture over more than 4,000 years. The significance is extremely important. The picture shows a corner of the exhibition hall.
